The interior, as glimpsed across the *Jessica Jones* (2016), *Power Man and Iron Fist*, and miscellaneous appearances: a working-class apartment laundered upward by Cage's modest income and Jones's PI receipts, dominated by Dani's accumulated material gravity — toys, books, a child-height shelf of stuffed animals that includes (across separate panels by separate artists) approximate likenesses of Squirrel Girl's Tippy-Toe, a generic Avengers-branded plush, and at least one item identifiable as Iron Fist–themed (a gift from Danny Rand, who is Dani's godfather in functional practice if not always in dialogue). Kitchen is the household's load-bearing room; the apartment lacks a dedicated office, with Jessica's case files migrating between kitchen table and bedroom depending on who is awake.

### 1.2 Developmental Status

Dani is currently rendered as a verbal preschooler — somewhere in the three-to-five-year band that Marvel sliding-timescale has held her at since approximately 2016. She is depicted as:

- **Linguistically forward.** Full sentences, narrative recall, the early capacity for sarcasm modeled directly off Jessica. Recent appearances show her correcting adult speech — a behavior pattern consistent with a child raised in a household where two articulate, verbally dominant adults treat her as a conversational participant.
- **Socially calm with strangers, including dangerous ones.** This is the most diagnostically interesting current behavioral datum. Children of her cohort, exposed to the parade of enhanced individuals that passes through her home, ought to display either stranger-anxiety escalation or indiscriminate friendliness; she displays neither. She greets, she observes, she withdraws to a parent if a read goes wrong. This is not normal four-year-old behavior. It is the early signature of the *operator's calm* that the adult timeline confirms in full bloom.
- **Physically robust but not yet visibly powered.** No on-panel feat of strength, no invulnerability event. Whether this reflects latency or absence is unresolved in canon; the adult record forces the inference of latency. Parental behavior — Luke does not modulate his strength around her in the way one modulates around a fragile child — suggests both parents either know or suspect she shares the inheritance.
- **Sleep and food patterns:** unremarkable on the page, which is itself canon-by-omission. A child with sleep disturbance in this household would generate plot; the absence of plot is the data.

### 1.3 Caregiving Network — Current Roster

The rotating in-loco-parentis network has narrowed compared to the Bendis-era *New Avengers* days but remains exceptional by civilian standards:

- **Squirrel Girl (Doreen Green):** Less frequent post-*Unbeatable Squirrel Girl* conclusion (2019), but still the household's emergency-call nanny. The relationship is canon-load-bearing; Dani's earliest extended caregiver outside her parents.
- **Danny Rand (Iron Fist):** Functional godfather, present at family events, occasional pickup duty.
- **Misty Knight and Colleen Wing:** Aunt-figures of operational standing, more present during the *Daughters of the Dragon*–era arcs.
- **Jessica Drew (Spider-Woman):** Reduced presence following Drew's own motherhood and her separate operational arc, but still in the trusted-contacts roster.
- **D.W. Griffith / supporting cast of the Cage solo runs:** Diminished post-Bendis but not erased.
- **The Defenders / street-level cohort (Daredevil, Iron Fist, Luke himself):** Functions as the deep bench. Daredevil's recent legal and identity turmoil has reduced his availability.

The adult-Dani's later capacity to bond instantly with a team-as-family (the U.S.Avengers integration) is *trained behavior* — this caregiving network is the training environment.

### 1.4 Recent Eventful Exposures (Child Timeline)

The child has been on the proximate edge of several recent civilizational disruptions without herself becoming a plot center:

- **The Hydra occupation of Manhattan (*Secret Empire*, 2017).** Luke and Jessica navigated the occupation with Dani in tow; Jessica's narration in adjacent material treats this period as the most acute decision-stress of the household's history.
- **The mayoralty of Wilson Fisk and *Devil's Reign* (2021–2022).** Anti-vigilante criminalization elevated household operational risk; Luke's eventual transition into the *mayoral* role himself (post–*Devil's Reign*) inverts the threat and creates a new exposure category — Dani is now, in the current setting, the child of a sitting New York mayor with a superhero past, which means civic-political threat surface on top of the prior super-criminal threat surface.
- **The Cage mayoralty (2022–present, *Mayor Luke Cage* / *Devil's Reign: Cage*).** This is the load-bearing recent development for the child-Dani's environment. Her father is now a public official. Her mother is now, by adjacency, a public official's spouse — a role Jessica is constitutionally unsuited for and which she has navigated by continuing private investigation work in defiance of the optics. Dani's exposure profile has shifted from *target of supercriminal opportunism* to *target of political and supercriminal opportunism*, and the household's security envelope has correspondingly thickened, with city resources now ambiguously available.
- **Krakoan and mutant-affairs adjacent events (2019–2024).** The household is non-mutant but operates in the Marvel-NYC space where Krakoan diplomacy, Orchis, and the fall of X mattered ambiently. No direct Dani involvement on record.

### 1.5 Current Functional Status (Child)

A small, watchful, verbally precocious child in a politically exposed superhero household, parented attentively by two adults whose careers have grown more rather than less demanding, with a caregiving bench of enhanced individuals on standby. No active threat to her on-record. No developmental concern on-record. The household is, by every available measure, functioning — which is the precondition the adult timeline requires to have happened, and which the adult timeline confirms did happen for long enough to produce the operator she becomes.

---

## 2. The Adult Clock — 20XX and the Multiversal Roster

### 2.1 Last Canonical Substantive Activity

The adult Captain America's last extended canonical arc remains the *U.S.Avengers* run (Ewing, 2017, twelve issues) and its *Generations: The Americas* coda, in which she shares a moment with Steve Rogers across timelines — narratively the closest the canon has come to letting her metabolize her inheritance against the original. Since the conclusion of that run, her appearances have been:

- Cameos and roster inclusions in the multiversal Avengers ensembles (the *Avengers Forever* / *Avengers Assemble* axis), where she is positioned as the Captain America of her thread among a council of variant Avengers.
- Background presence in the *Timeless* annuals and the Kang-related futures-survey material, where her timeline is one of several catalogued near-futures.
- Implicit reference whenever a present-day Cage-Jones scene reaches for thematic weight regarding Dani's potential.

She has not headlined a solo title. She has not been killed off. She has not been retconned. Her status is *active but in reserve* — the writers' room's behavior toward her resembles the household's behavior toward Dani: protective, episodic, the asset preserved for high-leverage deployment.

### 2.2 The Backstory as Currently Constituted

As the canon presently stands, the adult-Dani's path to the shield reads as follows. Her timeline diverges from the present-day mainline at an unspecified later point. In her thread, Steve Rogers dies or is permanently incapacitated. Luke Cage and Jessica Jones are dead by the time she takes the shield — the cause not specified in detail, the effect specified completely. She is trained by a surviving cohort that almost certainly includes Danny Rand (her godfather-in-practice) and likely figures from the Avengers Academy / next-generation pipeline. Her powers manifest along the inherited lines (super-strength at or exceeding Luke's, durability sufficient to absorb enhanced-tier strikes), with the shield as primary tool — a deliberate choice that subordinates inherited power to inherited principle.

She is recruited or pulled forward in time by Roberto Da Costa's organization, integrates within an operational tempo measured in hours, and runs missions in the present without leveraging her foreknowledge as a weapon against her parents' present-day selves. This last is the most important behavioral datum from the period: *she does not warn them*. She has the information; she does not use it. The discipline required for that omission is the entire psychological substance of the adult.

### 2.3 Current Status (Adult)

Catalogued in the multiversal Avengers reserve. Time-displaced or time-recurrent depending on the story. Carries the shield. Operationally healthy on-page. Emotionally unexamined off-page. The most recent appearances confirm the established affect baseline — composed, warm-on-demand, mission-first, past-tense about parents she has just seen alive in the room next door.

---

## 3. The Two Clocks in Mutual Pressure

### 3.1 The Recursion

Every recent issue featuring child-Dani is now read by the canon as backstory for the adult. Every recent issue featuring adult-Dani is read as fate-pressure on the child. This recursion has, over the last seven to ten years of publication, generated a specific aesthetic: the child's panels carry a weight disproportionate to her on-page action because the reader knows what she becomes; the adult's composure carries a weight disproportionate to her dialogue because the reader knows the small child whose loss it conceals.

The household — Luke and Jessica — operates in canon as if they do not know the adult timeline exists, though there are scattered references suggesting Luke at least has been briefed. The decision not to make this knowledge load-bearing is itself a writers'-room choice that protects the integrity of both clocks; were the parents to operate with full knowledge of their own deaths and their daughter's mantle, both timelines would collapse into a single overdetermined arc. The current canonical posture preserves the bifurcation, which preserves the subject.

### 3.2 How She Got Here (Child)

By being kept alive. Every recent crisis — Hydra occupation, mayoral takeover, the unceasing background of enhanced threat — has resolved with Dani still in the apartment, still with both parents, still on the trajectory the adult timeline requires. The household has paid the cost; she has been the protected variable. Luke's transition to the mayoralty is best read as a long-arc bet that he can do more for Dani's world from inside an institution than from outside it — the same theory of change his adult daughter will eventually adopt by taking the shield.

### 3.3 How She Got Here (Adult)

By losing everyone and refusing to break. The 20XX timeline is, in narrative function, the answer to the question *what is the worst case for this household, and does the child survive it intact?* The canon's answer is: the worst case happens, and she survives it not intact but *transformed* — into the symbol her parents' generation served. The path from the Harlem apartment to the shield is a path of subtraction (parents, Steve Rogers, the world she was raised in) followed by a single act of addition (taking up a principle larger than the people who taught it to her).

---

## 4. Current State — Synthesis

**Child-Dani, present day:** preschool-aged, verbally precocious, somatically robust, behaviorally calm beyond her years, embedded in a politically exposed superhero household whose threat profile has shifted upward with her father's mayoralty, surrounded by a thinned but still-exceptional caregiving network, and tracking — without anyone in the room saying so — toward a future the readers have already seen.

**Adult-Dani, displaced timeline:** active reserve in the multiversal Avengers apparatus, last fully developed in 2017, since then preserved in cameo and roster inclusion, status unchanged on the axes that matter — she still carries the shield, she still discusses her parents in past tense, she still has not used her foreknowledge to alter the past she came from. Her current operational tempo is episodic; her psychological status is the one this dossier has documented at length — high-functioning, mature-defenses, subclinical hyperresponsibility, an unprocessed grief contained by a role that requires the world to keep needing her.

**The subject as a single longitudinal entity:** a child currently being kept alive in Harlem by two parents whose love is doing exactly what it is supposed to do, and an adult currently keeping a country alive in a future where that love ran out. The recent history of both is the same history told from opposite ends. The current state of both is *holding*. The latent risk in both is *what happens if the structure that contains the grief — for the adult, the role; for the child, the parents — is removed*. For now, neither has been. The file remains open, and the subject, in both her instantiations, remains on the trajectory the evidence describes: load-bearing, by inheritance and by choice.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — DANIELLE CAGE

*Compiled longitudinally across both the present-day developmental record and the displaced 20XX adult record. Where canon is silent, the record notes inference and labels it as such; a full surveillance file does not pretend to ignorance, but it does flag where its certainty ends.*

---

## 1. Genetic and Constitutional Baseline

The subject inherits two non-baseline genomes, neither of them congenital in origin and both of them functionally heritable to a degree the canon has now confirmed.

**Paternal line (Carl Lucas — Burstein Process derivative).** Luke Cage's enhancements were acquired through an underground variant of the Burstein cell-regeneration / tissue-density experiment conducted in Seagate Prison. The process altered subdermal collagen, bone density, and myocyte cross-sectional strength, with collateral upregulation of healing factor. Whether such acquired traits are transmissible is a question Marvel biology answers empirically rather than mechanistically: the daughter manifests the trait, so the trait transmits. The likely mechanism — relevant for medical prediction — is germ-line cellular alteration concurrent with the somatic alteration, meaning Dani's cells were *born* Burstein-modified rather than acquiring the modification in utero or postnatally.

**Maternal line (Jessica Jones — Kree-augmented chemical exposure).** Jessica's super-strength and limited flight derive from a chemical spill of Kree origin sustained in adolescence. Again, the trait transmits: adult-Dani's strength baseline meets or exceeds both parents, and she has demonstrated flight-adjacent kinetics (high-velocity leap-and-glide, mid-air recovery) in 20XX-era panels.

**Net constitution.** The subject is, at the cellular level, a *double-substrate enhanced human* — Burstein-density tissues animated by Kree-grade strength output. The result is structurally novel: her father's body could not move at her speeds; her mother's body could not absorb her impacts. Dani is not a sum, she is a synthesis, and her body's tolerances exceed either parent's individually. This is the central medical fact of the file. Every other entry sits beneath it.

---

## 2. Perinatal and Neonatal Period

**Gestation.** Carried by Jessica Jones-Cage through a period (2005–2006 publication, in-universe contemporaneous with *House of M* aftermath and the *Civil War* lead-up) of extraordinary psychosocial stress and intermittent low-grade combat exposure. Jessica curtailed but did not eliminate vigilante activity. There is no canonical record of teratogenic exposure, abdominal trauma, or substance use during pregnancy; Jessica's documented relationship with alcohol pre-Cage was suspended during gestation (consistent with her on-page sobriety in the relevant arcs).

**Delivery.** Depicted in *The Pulse* #13 (2006). Hospital birth, Manhattan, attended by Doctor Strange, with Luke Cage and Jessica Drew present. Strange's involvement was prophylactic against mystical interference rather than obstetric need; the delivery itself proceeded without surgical intervention on record. Infant presented at apparent term, normal birthweight on-panel, immediate vocalization, no resuscitation indicated.

**APGAR-equivalent inference.** Within normal limits. The first weeks of life are depicted (Bendis run) with no NICU stay, no feeding difficulty, no jaundice noted. Breastfed (depicted on-panel, *New Avengers* vol. 2 incidental scenes).

**Cortisol environment.** High. The household's threat baseline through her neonatal weeks included federal scrutiny of Luke, an active Skrull infiltration not yet identified, and the parental decision-making load of where to physically locate the infant night-to-night. This does not constitute a *medical* event but does constitute a *neurodevelopmental* one, with HPA-axis implications likely contributing to the regulated-but-vigilant adult phenotype documented elsewhere in this file.

---

## 3. Infancy and Early Childhood — Discrete Events of Record

**The Jarvis-Skrull abduction (*Secret Invasion*, 2008).** The infant was handed by Jessica to a figure presenting as Edwin Jarvis, who was in fact a Skrull infiltrator. Physical recovery: complete, no injury sustained, no evidence of medical or surgical interference by the Skrull contingent. The episode is logged here rather than in the trauma section because of the *somatic* signature it almost certainly left on the household's caregiving behavior thereafter — handling protocols tightened, the infant was rarely transferred without two-adult verification, and Jessica's startle response to door-openings became a documented pattern through *New Avengers*. The infant absorbs this as ambient ritual; the body learns that the world's adults check each other before they accept her.

**Cosmic/dimensional exposures.** The Cage residence (Avengers Mansion, Avengers Tower, Harlem flat sequentially) was repeatedly the site of incursions through which the child was either present or proximate: Hood-aligned crime offensives, Norman Osborn's *Dark Reign* surveillance window, the *Siege* spillover from Asgard's fall, and *Fear Itself*'s Manhattan disturbances. No recorded injury. The negative finding is itself the datum: an exposure profile of this density without a single ER visit indicates an extraordinary protective envelope and, by inference, an unusually robust infant constitution. (The protective envelope is documentable; the constitutional robustness is inferred from absence of injury where injury was statistically overdetermined.)

**Childhood illnesses.** None of significance on record. Standard pediatric immunization status is not depicted; given Luke and Jessica's institutional skepticism balanced against Jessica's PI-grade pragmatism, full standard schedule is the working assumption.

**Dental, ophthalmologic, audiologic.** No record. No corrective devices ever depicted on either child-Dani or adult-Dani. Vision and hearing presumed normal-to-enhanced; adult operational performance is inconsistent with any uncorrected deficit.

**Growth and developmental milestones.** Verbal precocity documented (Walker's *Power Man and Iron Fist*, 2016 — multi-word utterance, contextual humor recognition by toddlerhood). Motor milestones unremarkable on-panel but inferentially advanced given subsequent adult capacity. Sleep architecture: the household's irregular hours and frequent night-time incidents almost certainly produced an *adaptable* rather than *fragile* sleep pattern — she would learn to sleep through sirens, fall asleep on adults in motion, and rouse quickly to alarm. This is a habit-of-body that will persist into adulthood.

---

## 4. Pubertal Window and Power Emergence (Inferred)

The canon does not depict Dani's adolescence directly. The adult subject's manifest enhancements require a transition window between the apparently-normal child of the present-day record and the fully-enhanced operator of 20XX. Three models are clinically plausible:

1. **Latent-then-pubertal expression.** Powers genetically encoded, expressed at hormonally-driven developmental windows (Marvel's most common mutant-adjacent pattern). Predicts a turbulent adolescence with sudden strength events, likely property damage, and a steep affect-regulation learning curve. Consistent with the controlled adult presentation only if a strong mentoring scaffold was present during emergence — and given the adult-timeline's parental loss, the *timing* of that loss relative to emergence becomes a critical and unrecorded variable.
2. **Gradual lifelong subclinical enhancement.** Powers present from birth at low expression, scaling with growth. Predicts a child who never broke a bone she should have, who was always slightly stronger than peers, who was carefully coached on calibration from preschool onward. Consistent with the absence of injury-record in childhood.
3. **Event-triggered onset.** Powers emerge in response to a traumatic precipitating event — most likely, the death of one or both parents. This model is dramatically congruent with the adult presentation (inheritance literalized) and would explain why the child reads as physically normal while the adult reads as a tier-1 enhanced. Clinically, it would also fuse the grief-event and the power-acquisition into a single non-separable identity-formative experience, which would predict exactly the introjective grief-resolution pattern documented in the psychological section.

The file's working assumption is a hybrid of (2) and (3): lifelong subclinical robustness explaining the injury-free childhood, with traumatic potentiation explaining the adult ceiling.

---

## 5. Adult Body — Operational Medical Profile (20XX Captain America Era)

**Anthropometrics.** Adult female, athletic build, presenting at a frame consistent with operational super-strength without grotesque hypertrophy — the Burstein/Kree synthesis produces strength via tissue density rather than mass, so her musculature is functional rather than displayed. She is heavier than she looks: estimated mass meaningfully above visual-baseline expectation due to subdermal density. (Relevant for transport, restraint, and any platform she stands on.)

**Tissue integrity.** Subdermal layer impervious to small-arms fire on the order of her father's documented tolerances; canon depictions show her absorbing blunt-force trauma from enhanced opponents without dermal breach. Knife and conventional projectile wounds: not sustained on record. Energy weapons: she has taken energy-grade hits and continued operating, though the depth of tolerance is not stress-tested in canon.

**Healing factor.** Inferred at or near her father's rate. No depicted convalescence period across her appearances. Bruising depicted minimally; resolution timing not on-panel.

**Strength output.** Demonstrated lifting/throwing at the upper end of the street-level enhanced tier. Has wielded the shield (vibranium, mass non-trivial) one-handed at speed and accuracy comparable to Steve Rogers' operational record. No on-panel ceiling test.

**Cardiovascular and pulmonary.** Sustained-engagement endurance well above human baseline. No depicted exhaustion event.

**Pain perception.** This is the medically interesting finding. The Burstein-derived dermal armor effectively eliminates a category of pain signals that, in baseline humans, function as the somatic brake on aggression and the early-warning for retreat. The subject must regulate threat-response by *cognition* rather than by *interoception*. Two operational consequences: (a) she can press through injury she has not yet noticed, (b) she does not feel the body-level fatigue cues that normally cap operator tempo. Clinical implication: the subject is at elevated risk of *unrecognized internal injury* (anything penetrating the dermal layer would bypass the body's external warning system and present late) and at elevated risk of *cumulative wear* in joints and tendons that her own healing factor may or may not fully repair.

**Nutritional and metabolic.** Caloric requirements presumed elevated consistent with her output; not depicted. No eating disorder pattern, no body-image content in canon. Hydration unremarkable.

**Reproductive.** No pregnancy, no contraceptive regimen, no gynecological event on record. The medical question of whether her dual-enhanced genome could safely gestate is unaddressed in canon and not a file priority.

**Substance exposure.** Negative across the record. No alcohol use depicted (notable given maternal pattern — the avoidance reads as *informed*, not naive). No tobacco, no recreational drugs, no performance enhancers. Caffeine: presumed standard operator-tier use, not depicted.

**Sleep.** Operational. The childhood-acquired ability to sleep through alarm and wake clean to alert persists. Probable chronic mild sleep debt under heavy mission tempo, consistent with the cohort.

**Menstrual cycle, endocrine function, immune profile.** Unrecorded. Inferentially within enhanced-baseline ranges, with the expected immune robustness of a Burstein-derivative subject.

---

## 6. Surgeries, Transformations, and Procedures

**Surgical history.** None on record, child or adult. The dermal-density of the adult subject would make conventional surgical access non-trivial — a fact relevant to any future emergency medical planning. Her father's medical record contains documented difficulty of surgical intervention; the same constraints apply, plausibly more strictly, to her.

**Transformations.** No depicted bodily transformation event — no symbiote bonding, no cosmic upgrade, no mystical possession on record. She is, unusually for her cohort, *one body throughout*. This is itself a medically protective fact: she does not carry the metabolic and psychological aftermath of repeated radical somatic change that operators of her tier typically accumulate.

**Time displacement.** The single great transformation of her record is not biological but *chronological*: removal from her native 20XX timeline and insertion into the present. The body experienced no documented physiological cost from the displacement itself. The psychiatric cost is logged elsewhere.

**Devices and implants.** None. The shield is not an implant; it is a tool. She carries no comms hardware that the canon depicts as permanent; no tracking, no augmentic, no prosthetic. Her body is unaccessorized.

---

## 7. Disability and Functional Limitation

None on record. The negative finding is comprehensive: no documented sensory deficit, no documented motor limitation, no documented cognitive impairment, no documented chronic condition. This is unusual enough across her cohort to warrant suspicion of *underreporting* rather than absence — combat operators at her tempo accumulate microinjuries that go undocumented, and her healing factor would mask many. The likely true picture: a body operating without complaint at the cost of complaints it cannot feel.

---

## 8. Psychological Impact of the Medical Record

**The injury-free childhood.** A child who is never seriously hurt in an environment that should hurt her develops an unspoken sense of bodily invulnerability that is *almost* correct. This produces, in adulthood, a calibration problem: she has no childhood somatic memory of *being broken*, which makes her excellent at acting through threat and weak at recognizing the moment threat has become injury. The body's own history has never taught her to fear it.

**The two genomes and the question of "what am I."** Most enhanced individuals can locate the origin of their condition in a single event — an accident, an experiment, a bite. Dani's enhancement is *inherited*, which is rarer in her cohort and psychologically distinct. She did not become; she was. There is no pre-enhanced self to grieve and no acquisition trauma to integrate. This is a quiet protective factor against the identity-fragmentation that plagues her peers. Her body has always been her body.

**The pain-perception gap and ethical compensation.** Because her body does not give her the somatic cues that brake aggression in baseline humans, the *ethical* brake has to be conscious. She has built one — the principled, cognition-mediated, value-anchored restraint that defines her operational presentation. The medical fact undergirds the moral architecture: she is principled in part because her body cannot afford her to be otherwise.

**The healing factor and the deferred reckoning.** A body that heals quickly accumulates an unprocessed catalogue of what it has survived. There is no convalescence in which to integrate what happened. The injuries do not become memories the way they do for baseline operators, who lie still and think while they mend. Dani has no scar archive; the cost-of-mission ledger that other operators keep in their bodies, she must keep — if at all — in her mind. The same architecture that protects her body from breaking protects her grief from being felt at body level, and this is the *medical* substrate of the deferred reckoning logged in the psychiatric section.

**The negative findings, considered as a class.** No illness, no injury, no surgery, no substance, no disability, no transformation. The file's medical history reads as the cleanest in her cohort. This is not an oversight; it is a finding. The subject's body has been the most consistently *unreported* asset she has, and a surveillance file's proper response to a perfectly clean record is to note the asymmetry: a person at her exposure level whose body has nothing to say has either been extraordinarily fortunate, extraordinarily protected, or extraordinarily good at not letting the body speak. The working assessment is *all three*, in that order, with the third growing in weight as she ages into her role.

---

*End Section 2 of file. Cross-reference: §3 Psychological, §4 Psychiatric for the affective consequences of the pain-perception architecture documented above; §5 Personality for the operational behaviors that follow from a body that does not flinch.*


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS: DANIELLE CAGE

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across both developmental phases. Where child-record and adult-record diverge, both are noted; where adult patterns appear to be matured continuations of childhood tells, the through-line is traced.*

---

## I. Build, Frame, and Resting Carriage

The adult subject stands approximately 5'9"–5'10", framed long through the femur and the trapezius — taller than her mother, shorter than her father, with the long-muscle distribution of someone whose strength is endogenous rather than weight-trained. Shoulder girdle wide, clavicles set high and level (no chronic asymmetry from preferred-side load-bearing — a tell that her strength is bilateral and uncoached). Hips narrow relative to shoulder span. Hands large, fingers long, knuckles unremarkable despite combat exposure (subdermal durability prevents the boxer's-knuckle hypertrophy that would normally accompany her hit-rate). Neck thick at the base, consistent with inherited musculature; jaw set wide at the masseter, a feature she shares with Luke, though softened by Jessica's cheekbone architecture.

Resting weight distribution is even: feet shoulder-width when standing in conversation, weight on the whole foot rather than the heel, knees soft. She does not lock her knees in formal contexts — a small operational habit (locked knees impede a rapid drop-step) that has become postural default. When she has to stand still for protocol — debrief lines, photo ops, ceremony — the stillness is *active*, a small isometric engagement through the glutes and core, never the slumped patience of a civilian.

The child, at toddler and early-school ages, was already noted by household observers (Squirrel Skirts, Jarvis, Drew) as physically *settled* — a child who did not fidget in laps, who could sit through long adult conversations without squirming. The adult carriage is the child-stillness scaled up.

---

## II. Gait and Movement Signature

**Gait.** Long, even-cadenced, slightly heel-first but with a quick roll-through; pace approximately 115 steps/min unaccompanied, dropping to match civilian companions without visible effort. She does not walk on the balls of her feet (no infantry-school overlay) nor with the rolling shoulders of a fighter advertising himself — her movement does not telegraph. In Harlem foot-traffic (present-day visits with her child-self's parents) she moves at the local cadence; in DC corridors she lengthens stride to match institutional pace. This is unconscious mirroring and one of her most consistent unconscious tells: she calibrates gait to environment within ten paces.

**Threat-state gait.** Stride shortens by perhaps fifteen percent, weight transfers forward of center, the heel-strike disappears entirely and the foot lands midfoot-flat. Arms drop from the natural pendulum to a quieter carriage with elbows fractionally bent — hands available. The shoulders do not rise; rising shoulders are a civilian threat-tell and she has trained it out (or, more likely, never had it: Luke does not raise his shoulders under threat either). Head carriage drops perhaps one degree, chin tucked a fraction — protection of the throat that reads as nothing to a layman and as a fighter's posture to anyone who has seen one.

**Movement at speed.** Running, she is efficient rather than fast-looking; long stride, low vertical oscillation, arms loose. In combat motion, she is — by inheritance — capable of impact-redirection movements that would shatter a normal pelvis. She does not throw herself into hits the way her father does; she is closer to her mother's *line-of-force* style, stepping inside the arc, breaking distance rather than absorbing it. Her body knows it can absorb; her training has decided that absorption is wasteful.

**Sit-down pattern.** She sits *backward into* a chair (controlled descent, back muscles braking) rather than dropping. She does not cross her legs at the knee in operational settings; either both feet flat or one ankle on the opposite knee (the open, ready posture). At rest with family she will tuck a foot under herself on a couch — a regression-to-childhood posture observed in adult-Dani during her time-displaced stays in the Cage household.

---

## III. Hands

**Resting position.** Hands open, fingers slightly curled, thumbs not tucked. She does not clench in repose. The default is "available" — a hand-position that costs zero milliseconds to weaponize and looks like nothing.

**Gestural vocabulary.** She speaks with restrained hand-emphasis: small flat-palm gestures at the level of her own sternum, occasionally one open-hand sweep to indicate inclusion of a group. She does not point with the index finger (a deliberate-looking suppression, possibly trained out by Steve Rogers' canonical teaching style in her timeline, possibly learned from Luke's similar suppression — pointing reads as aggression to people who have been on the wrong end of authority). When she does need to indicate, she uses the whole open hand, palm angled up.

**Tics, self-touch, micro-gestures.**
- Periodic right-thumb-across-left-knuckles, a slow soothing pass, usually when listening. This is observable from late toddlerhood — the child version was thumb-across-the-back-of-her-mother's-hand when held. It has migrated to self.
- Touches the shield's edge — when wearing it — at a specific point on the inner curve, with the pad of the right index finger. A grounding contact, performed unconsciously roughly every ninety seconds in stressful contexts.
- When the shield is off her arm, the same gesture transfers: index-finger pad finds the inside of her own opposite wrist, on the radial pulse. She is, without knowing it, taking her own pulse for reassurance.
- Does not bite nails, does not pick at cuticles, does not chew the inside of her cheek. The mouth is *uncolonized* by anxiety — itself notable, and consistent with a child whose oral-stage anxieties were well-met.
- The single oral micro-tell: a brief pursing of the lower lip, drawn slightly inward, when she is being told something she will not contradict but does not accept. Read across appearances, this is her *disagreement-held* signal.

**Hands in intimacy.** With family (the present-day parents she has buried in her own timeline), her hands betray what her face does not: she touches them more than is necessary. A hand on Jessica's shoulder lingers a half-second past the social beat; a hand grasping Luke's forearm for a hello-grip does not release for an extra count. She is not aware she does this. It is the only place the grief leaks.

---

## IV. Face: Resting, Speaking, Listening

**Resting face.** Even, slightly grave, eyes soft rather than narrowed — what a stranger reads as "kind but serious." The default mouth is *neutral-closed*, lips relaxed, no compression. The forehead is unlined for her apparent age, suggesting low chronic brow engagement; she does not furrow under thought, she furrows only under decision.

**Smile.** Two distinct smiles on record.
- *Operational smile* — symmetrical, brief, eyes engaged but not crinkled, used in greetings, civilian-reassurance, photo settings. Holds approximately 1.5 seconds, releases cleanly.
- *Earned smile* — asymmetric, slightly higher on the left, eye-crinkle present, a small head-duck. Reserved for: teammates after shared completion of a hard piece of work, her father (both timelines), small children, and her mother when her mother is being acerbic. The asymmetry is inherited (Jessica smiles the same way) but the head-duck is hers alone.

**Listening face.** Eyes hold the speaker, head slightly tilted toward the dominant ear (right), the chin micro-tucks at points of agreement, lifts a fraction at points of disagreement she does not voice. She blinks less than baseline when listening attentively — approximately 8–10 blinks/min versus a normal 15–20 — a sustained-attention signature observed in police-trained and military observers. This is not from formal training; it is the same look the child gave adults from age three onward, a precocious watchfulness her parents both commented on.

**Speaking face.** Mouth movements are economical, words don't spill, the jaw stays soft. She does not over-articulate. Eyebrow movement is minimal and concentrated on emphasis verbs — the inheritance here is Luke's: a face that does not waste motion.

**Threat-state face.** Affect *compresses* rather than tightens. The expressive band narrows; the face becomes a *cooler* version of itself rather than a tenser one. Eyes harden one stop, mouth goes from neutral-closed to neutral-set, micro-expressions cease. To untrained observers she looks *calmer* under threat than at rest — a deeply misleading signal, and one of her most operationally valuable traits.

**Grief micro-expression.** A specific, brief pattern: a downward flick of the gaze (not full eye-closure), a single slow exhale through the nose, return. Observed when present-day Luke or Jessica enters a room she is in, before she has composed her greeting. Lasts approximately 600 milliseconds. The recovery is total and immediate.

---

## V. Eyes and Gaze Architecture

**Scan pattern.** On entering an unfamiliar room: door behind her noted, then a counter-clockwise sweep covering high corners, then exits, then bodies present, then surfaces (objects that could become weapons or cover). The whole sweep takes under two seconds and reads as a casual look-around. This is the room-entry sequence taught by no specific instructor in her history — it appears to be a synthesis of her mother's PI-trained pattern and her father's prison-trained periphery awareness. She has been doing it since she was old enough to walk through doorways unaided.

**Fixation.** Steady. She does not glance-away under direct eye contact; she holds and softens. Under interrogation-like pressure (formal inquiry, hostile questioning), the gaze becomes a *flat* hold — neither aggressive nor evasive, the look of someone who has decided the conversation is happening to her rather than with her.

**Peripheral usage.** Demonstrably wide. In observable instances she has tracked off-axis motion at her four o'clock without head-turning, a habit consistent with someone who learned early that the threat may come from where you are not looking. This is the trained inheritance of being a Cage-Jones household child.

**Pupillary response.** Normal in regulated conditions. In moments of decision under stress, observable mydriasis is present but recovers quickly — not the locked-dilated stare of true panic.

---

## VI. Voice and Vocal Architecture

**Pitch.** Lower-mid alto, with a chest-resonance that carries without volume — she does not need to raise her voice to be heard across a room. The placement is *forward*, the consonants crisp without being percussive. There is a slight Harlem flattening on certain vowels — the "a" in *family*, the "o" in *gone* — inherited from both parents and not eroded by adult institutional environments. She has not been trained out of where she comes from.

**Cadence.** Measured, with brief considered pauses before substantive answers, no verbal filler ("um," "like," "you know" — all near-absent). When she does pause, it is silent rather than filled. This is unusual and reads as authority to listeners; it is also a tell — the absence of filler indicates a habitual cognitive economy, a person who would rather say nothing for two seconds than say something useless.

**Volume range.** Narrow. Her command voice is not loud, it is *placed*; her intimate voice is not soft, it is *slowed*. The range of vocal volume she uses across a day spans perhaps fifteen decibels, where a typical adult uses thirty. This is a control trait shared with her father, who similarly under-modulates.

**Laugh.** Real, low, surprised-sounding when it happens — she does not perform laughter. A genuine laugh from her is brief (two or three pulses), drops the chin, recovers quickly. Polite laughter she does not produce; she will instead offer the operational smile.

**Voice under threat.** Drops half a step in pitch, slows by about ten percent, becomes more declarative. Imperative sentences shorten ("Down." "With me." "Not yet."). She does not yell in combat; the volume stays at conversational and the *clarity* increases. People do what she says because the voice does not give them the option of misunderstanding.

**Voice with family.** Higher by a half-step, more melodic, more diminutives. She calls present-day Luke "Dad" with a half-beat of hesitation before the word — every time, observably — as if recalibrating which version of him she is addressing.

---

## VII. Breath and Autonomic Pattern

Resting respiration is slow — approximately 11–13 breaths/min, low diaphragmatic, with a long quiet exhale. This is athlete-baseline and approaches contemplative-practitioner range. Under acute stress, the rate does not climb the way a civilian's would; instead the *depth* increases first, the rate second. She has a specific re-set she performs unconsciously: one long nasal inhale (approximately four seconds), held for one, released through pursed lips for approximately six — a physiological vagal-tone exercise that she does not appear to have been formally taught. It happens roughly twice per hour in operational settings, more frequently after decisions involving the loss or risk to a teammate.

Heart rate, where observable through carotid visibility in combat tape: ~55 resting, climbs to perhaps 110 in heavy engagement and recovers within ninety seconds of disengagement. This is below combat-medic norms for her exertion level — partly inheritance, partly conditioning.

The autonomic system is well-regulated *with one exception*: in the presence of her present-day living parents, a small persistent elevation is detectable — slight increase in resting respiratory rate (one or two breaths/min higher), slight increase in baseline muscle tone in the shoulders, a faint flush at the neck visible in good light. Her body, more honest than her composure, knows it is in the presence of the dead.

---

## VIII. Grooming, Self-Maintenance, and Personal Inventory

**Hair.** Worn natural in childhood (a household photographic record), in adulthood pulled back functionally — typically a low bun or a tight braid for operations, released for off-duty hours. The transitions between styles are quick and unfussy; she does not adjust her hair in mirrors compulsively. She does check her own reflection on entry to bathrooms — a sweep more diagnostic than vain (any blood, any disorder of kit).

**Skin and face.** Minimal product use, no cosmetic ornamentation in operational contexts; an unstudied moisturizing routine inherited from her mother's no-nonsense regimen. No piercings beyond perhaps a single set of ear-lobe holes, often unworn. No tattoos in canonical depiction — a small but significant absence: a generation of operators marks itself, and she does not. The body is not narrativized externally; the symbols she carries are removable (the shield, the uniform).

**Nails.** Short, filed clean, unpolished in operational windows. She trims them herself; the trim is even, suggesting bilateral fine-motor control unaffected by power-set asymmetry.

**Scent.** Soap-and-clean baseline, no fragrance worn in operations (a tactical discipline), occasional civilian use of a light citrus when off-duty. Her father's preference profile is similar.

**Inventory carried on body, off-uniform.** Wallet (slim, back pocket — not back-pocket-civilian, more like the front-of-the-back-pocket position that resists pickpocketing), a phone (held in the non-dominant hand by default, leaving the strong side free), keys arranged with a single longer one protruding between the fingers when held — a defensive habit observable even when she is in friendly territory. A small folding knife or its equivalent is almost always somewhere on her person; she does not feel undressed without the shield, but she feels *uncalibrated* without a blade.

**On-uniform inventory.** The shield is the primary, but observation shows she keeps a backup of small functional items: medical kit on the left rear of the belt, comms on the right, no decorative additions, no trophies. She does not name her gear.

---

## IX. Sleep Architecture

Sleep onset is fast — under ten minutes — *on her own terms*, in a space she has cleared. The clearing is itself a ritual: door checked twice (the second check happens after she has begun to undress, an interrupting check that suggests the first did not fully discharge the vigilance), windows assessed for sight-lines, the shield (or substitute weapon) placed within arm's reach of the dominant hand. The room she sleeps in best is one she has slept in before; novel rooms add fifteen to thirty minutes to onset.

Sleep position default: on her back, one arm slightly out from the body on the dominant side, the other across the abdomen. She does not curl. The back-sleep is unusual for a woman of her cohort and is consistent with someone who needs to be able to come upright in a single motion. Side-sleep occurs only in environments she trusts completely — the present-day Cage apartment is one such environment, observable across multiple stays.

Sleep duration: approximately six and a half hours, consolidated, with one brief wake near the three-hour mark — a head-lift, a sweep of the room, a settle. The wake-and-sweep is so brief it would not register on most monitoring; it is visible only in long-form video review.

Dream activity: not directly observable, but indirect evidence (post-wake affect, occasional reports to teammates) suggests vivid dreaming with a recurrent setting featuring her parents in motion. She does not describe these as nightmares. She does not describe them at all unless asked.

Wake-up: clean, single motion, no snooze pattern, feet on floor within thirty seconds of consciousness. She does not lie in bed thinking.

---

## X. Eating and Hydration

**Caloric load.** Inherited musculature with elevated metabolic baseline requires substantially above-average intake — observably she eats roughly twice the volume of a civilian her size without weight gain. Her father's pattern is similar.

**Style.** Fast, focused, efficient when alone — a working-meal pattern that does not linger. Slow, conversational, second-helping when with family. The shift is dramatic and observable: with the present-day Cage-Jones household she will sit at table for ninety minutes over a meal she could clear in fifteen. The duration is the point.

**Preferences.** Inherits her father's palate (Southern home-cooking lineage, slow-cooked proteins, carbohydrate-dense starches) and her mother's coffee dependency (taken black, in volume, throughout the operational day). She does not drink alcohol in any observed instance — a notable absence in a peer group that uses it heavily for decompression. The cleanest read of this abstinence is *operational hygiene*; a secondary read is that she has watched her mother's relationship with whiskey closely enough to have made a private decision.

**Hydration.** Constant, low-volume sipping throughout the day rather than scheduled intake — a self-regulating habit. Water bottle near to hand at all times in operational environments.

**Stress eating.** Does not, observably. Stress *suppresses* her appetite — she will go hours past normal mealtime without noticing in a crisis window, and has to be reminded by teammates. This is a vulnerability she does not acknowledge.

---

## XI. Sexual and Intimate Somatic Register

No partnered sexual history is on canonical record. The absence is itself a datum — by her chronological adult years, the absence of a documented partnership is a structural feature of her life rather than a gap in observation. The inferential read: intimate availability is bottlenecked not by orientation or desire but by *mission-saturation* and by the un-tested competency of low-stakes one-to-one bonding identified in the psychological workup.

What can be observed of her physical comfort with intimacy: she initiates physical contact with trusted figures (a hand on the shoulder, the briefly held forearm), accepts hugs without stiffening, returns them with appropriate pressure and duration. There is no aversion pattern, no flinch-from-touch, no over-controlled boundary. The bodily readiness for intimacy is intact; the situational opportunity is not present in the canonical window. Her body knows how to be held. It is not, currently, often being held.

In the presence of children (her own younger self, in displaced-timeline contact; teammates' children), her body softens further than in any other observed context — shoulders drop, voice lowers, hands open palm-up. This is the most-deregulated affect she exhibits.

---

## XII. Pain, Injury, and Somatic Cost

The body does not break, but it is not unsignalled. Observable post-combat tells include: slow rotation of the right shoulder (a habitual loosening, not an injury — the same shoulder that takes the shield's impact reaction), brief stretching of the cervical spine with a small audible release, and a pattern of pressing the heel of the hand into the low back when she thinks she is unobserved. The latter is the one place chronic load accumulates — the shield-bearer's lumbar signature, identical to one of Steve Rogers' tells.

She does not vocalize discomfort. The absence of pain-vocalization is so consistent that teammates have learned to read her *silence about a wound* as the indicator that a wound is present.

The cost the somatic atlas documents most clearly: she carries no visible scars, no acquired asymmetries, no chronic injuries — and yet she carries a body that has, in her timeline, watched two parents die and a nation collapse around it. The somatic record of that history is not in the skin. It is in the door-check repeated twice, the wrist-pulse-touch every ninety seconds, the half-beat hesitation before the word *Dad*, and the back-sleep with the weapon-hand free. The body keeps the score the chart cannot.

---

## XIII. State-Shift Summary

| Domain | Calm | Stress | Threat | Intimacy |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Posture | Settled, weight whole-foot | Forward shift, knees soften | Compressed forward, chin tuck | Open, shoulders drop |
| Gait | 115/min, heel-roll | Shortened, midfoot | Quiet, arms available | Loose, ambling |
| Face | Neutral-soft | Neutral-set | Cooler, micro-expression off | Asymmetric smile, head-duck |
| Eyes | Soft, room-sweep on entry | Wider scan radius | Flat hold, peripheral on | Direct, lingering |
| Voice | Mid-alto, low filler | Slower, more declarative | Half-step lower, imperative | Half-step higher, melodic |
| Breath | 11–13/min | Depth-first increase | Vagal re-set deployed | Slowed, deeper |
| Hands | Open, available | Wrist-pulse contact | Empty, ready | Reaching, lingering |
| Mouth | Closed-neutral | Lip-purse on disagreement | Set, silent | Slight smile-rest |

The pattern across the table: her body *compresses inward and downward* under threat (smaller, lower, quieter) and *opens outward and upward* in intimacy (taller, warmer, slower). Stress is the in-between state where the compression has begun but not completed, and where most of her observable tells live. She is hardest to read when she is in actual danger and easiest to read when she is being loved. This is the somatic signature of a person whose defenses were built for combat and whose defenses for being cared for were never finished.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# Attachment & Relational Patterns

## I. The Foundational Imprint: Two Survivors Loving Competently

To understand how Danielle Cage bonds — at six months, at six years, at twenty-six in a borrowed shield — one has to begin with what the perinatal record actually shows, which is rarer than the file's surface chaos suggests: *two trauma survivors who managed to love a child well*. This is not the default outcome for parents with Jessica's and Luke's etiologies. Jessica is a rape and mind-control survivor whose pre-Dani interpersonal baseline was caustic, avoidant, alcohol-mediated, and committed to a low-trust read of nearly every person who entered her orbit. Luke is a man whose formative adult years were stolen in Seagate, whose body was modified without informed consent, whose default mode is wariness compressed into stillness. The statistical expectation, given those two histories converging on an infant, is some combination of inconsistent availability, intrusive vigilance, and the subtle communication to the child that *you are the reason we are afraid now*.

What the longitudinal record actually shows is the opposite. Luke in the *New Avengers* and *Power Man and Iron Fist* sequences is a tactile father — physical contact constant, voice modulated downward in her presence, body angled to put himself between her and any sightline he has not cleared. Jessica's *Pulse* and *Jessica Jones* (2016) appearances depict a mother whose default sarcasm flattens into a different register entirely when Dani is in the frame: present, declarative, descriptive ("you're okay, you're with me, that's the door, that's Daddy"). Neither parent performs parenthood; both *do* it, on the operational level of moment-to-moment attunement. The attachment-research term is *earned secure base*: caregivers who were not securely attached themselves but who, through effortful conscious work, deliver secure attachment to the child.

This is the foundation. Everything subsequent — every adult relational pattern, every trust-quick / disclose-slow asymmetry, every chosen-family reflex — runs on this footing. **The subject was loved well, on purpose, by people who knew exactly how badly love can be done.**

## II. The Distributed Caregiver Network and Its Long Tail

The second formative variable is structural: Dani's primary caregivers were augmented — and at times outright substituted — by a rotating roster of superhuman adjuncts. Squirrel Girl as live-in nanny during the *New Avengers* vol. 2 period. Jarvis (the real one, post-Skrull-recovery) as a near-grandparental fixture. Jessica Drew, Iron Fist, Wolverine, and various Avengers-tower personnel cycling through in loco parentis windows when both parents were called out. This is not occasional babysitting; this is a *committee* model of safety in which the dyadic mother-father-child triangle is structurally embedded in a larger holding environment.

The developmental consequence is precise and visible in the adult record. Most securely attached children internalize a working model that runs: *one or two people are the source of safety; everyone else is conditional*. Dani's working model runs differently: *safety is a property of a competent group I am inside of*. Her trust generalizes faster than baseline, her perimeter accommodates more people faster, and her relational economy treats the team as the unit of attachment rather than any individual within it. In *U.S.Avengers*, she integrates into Roberto Da Costa's outfit not over weeks but over a handful of operations — and the integration is not professional politeness, it is *kin-coding*: she calls them by working names quickly, she reads their patterns, she covers for them without negotiation. This is the Squirrel-Girl-and-Jarvis-and-Jessica-Drew model running in adult mode. The child who was rocked to sleep by four different superhumans in any given week did not learn to need one person; she learned to need *the room being full of the right people*.

There is a cost to this pattern, and the file should mark it. Distributed attachment trades depth for breadth. Dani is, on present evidence, exceptional at *team* intimacy and underdeveloped at *dyadic* intimacy. The one-to-one relationship — the partner, the confidant, the person to whom one tells the things one does not tell the team — is not, in any canonical appearance, a competency she demonstrates. Her models for that register are her parents, whose dyadic bond was forged in shared combat and mutual rescue and is, frankly, atypical. She has never seen ordinary intimacy modeled. She has seen *foxhole* intimacy modeled and has no internal map for anything else.

## III. The Hypervigilant Substrate Beneath the Secure Surface

The third foundational variable is the *ambient threat field* of her infancy. Skrull infiltration of the household (the Jarvis abduction — recovered, but ontologically destabilizing for the mother and, through her, for the child's pre-verbal emotional weather). Repeated discussions, overheard or absorbed osmotically, of whether to send her away. Stash-houses. Cover stories. Faked separations used as tradecraft. The *Jessica Jones* (2016) opening, in which Dani is temporarily removed from the home under a fabricated marital-separation cover to bait an enemy, is paradigmatic: even in toddlerhood, she is a *piece on the board*, moved by her mother for protective reasons but moved nonetheless.

A child raised this way encodes a specific dual signal: *I am loved fiercely; I am also negotiable when the situation requires it*. This is not pathogenic in itself — the love half is real and consistent — but it produces a relational style in which the subject *expects* to be moved by larger considerations and in which she, in turn, accepts being part of others' calculus. She does not take it personally when a teammate disappears for mission reasons. She does not require constant reaffirmation. She also, more subtly, will *move herself* — withdraw, redeploy, take the harder post — for the team's good without registering this as sacrifice. It is just what people in her family do. The Atlas-pattern hyperresponsibility noted in the psychiatric section originates here: the toddler who watched her parents reorganize their entire lives around her safety internalized the lesson that *the structure adapts to protect the vulnerable*, and grew into the adult who reflexively volunteers to be the structure.

## IV. How She Bonds

Bonding, for the subject, proceeds in a characteristic four-beat sequence that is observable across her child appearances (in proto-form, with toys and Avengers personnel) and her adult ones (with the U.S.Avengers, with present-day Luke and Jessica, with Steve Rogers in *Generations*).

**Beat one: rapid behavioral read.** Within minutes of meeting a new person, she has clocked their movement economy, their threat baseline, their tells. This is direct inheritance from Jessica (PI-trained surveillance habit) compounded by a childhood spent reading whether the adult walking into the apartment was the real one. She does this without performing it.

**Beat two: functional trust extended provisionally.** She will work alongside the new person at full operational commitment immediately, on the working assumption that they are who they appear to be. This *looks* like fast trust and is often misread as such by recipients. It is not. It is *fast functional cooperation*, which is a different thing. She is loaning the relationship her competence, not her interior.

**Beat three: pattern-confirmation over repeated stress events.** Across multiple operations, she watches whether the person holds under pressure, whether their stated values track their behavior under cost, whether they protect the vulnerable when it is expensive. This is a long evaluation, often months in subjective time. The recipient usually does not know they are being assessed; the assessment is silent.

**Beat four: kin-coding.** If the pattern confirms, she promotes the person to family — and the promotion is *invisible to the recipient* because the surface behavior changes very little. What changes is the internal ledger: she will now bleed for them without calculation, take career-ending risks for their reputations, mourn them with the introjective intensity that defines her grief style. The person rarely knows they have been admitted until something costs Dani to honor it.

This four-beat sequence is the operative pattern in every significant relationship she has on record. It is efficient, low-friction, and produces few bad bonds. It also has a structural blind spot: the *between-team* relationship — the friend who is not a colleague, the lover who is not a co-operator — has no slot in the sequence. Beat two ("functional trust through shared task") cannot fire if there is no shared task. The sequence stalls, and what reads externally as romantic guardedness or social reticence is in fact a *bonding apparatus with no protocol for non-mission contexts*.

## V. How She Distrusts

Distrust, when it forms, is not noisy. There is no rupture event, no confrontation, no expressed-emotion spike. The pattern, traceable in her mother's behavior and clearly inherited, is *quiet declassification*: the person is silently demoted in the internal ledger, the four-beat sequence is reset to beat two for them specifically, and Dani's full operational competence remains available to them while her interior is withdrawn. They will not notice. They are not supposed to notice. The withdrawal is not punitive — it is protective, and it is the same mechanism Jessica uses with people who have failed her assessment but whom she still has to work with.

The triggers for declassification, derivable from her parents' modeled patterns and her own canonical responses to betrayal events in the broader Avengers network, are narrow and specific:

- *Failure to protect the vulnerable when it costs the person something.* Cowardice in the face of the wrong cost is the unforgivable.
- *Use of a vulnerable third party as leverage.* The Skrull-Jarvis imprint, transmitted through her mother's response to it, makes this the most charged category.
- *Pattern-incongruence between stated values and observed behavior under stress.* Hypocrisy under cost. The values do not have to be hers; they have to be the person's own, consistently held.
- *Lying about anything that affects the operational picture.* Lying about personal matters is forgivable and often expected. Lying about the field is not.

What is *not* on the list is also informative: she does not declassify for ideological disagreement, for personality friction, for past mistakes honestly owned, or for failures of competence (as opposed to failures of will). Her trust criteria are *behavioral* and *ethical*, not stylistic or doctrinal. This is Luke's framework operating in her — the Harlem code that judges men by what they do under pressure, not by what they believe at rest.

## VI. How She Is Betrayed, and How She Repairs

Betrayal hits her in a specific somatic and cognitive register. Because her body does not break, the impact of betrayal cannot route through the physiological pain-signaling that normally accompanies relational injury in baseline humans. The interoceptive signal — *this hurts, retreat* — is muted. What she gets instead is a cognitive shutdown of the kin-coding: the person is excised from the family ledger, often before she has consciously decided to excise them. The subjective experience, inferable from her affect in canonical betrayal-adjacent moments, is of *suddenly noticing that someone has already become a stranger*. The processing has happened underneath conscious access; she is informed of its outcome.

This is, clinically, a high-functioning but expensive defense. It prevents the prolonged ambivalence that wrecks most relational injuries — she does not relitigate, she does not oscillate, she does not return to the wound. It also forecloses repair in cases where repair would be possible and valuable. The excised person, in her ledger, has to re-enter at beat one, and the re-entry is rare; the assessment system trusts its prior verdict.

Repair, when it does happen, follows her father's modeled pattern rather than her mother's. Luke's repair style is *long sustained presence* — he does not apologize verbally so much as he shows up, repeatedly, in the work, over time, until the relationship has been re-knit by accreted action. Dani's repair gestures, observable in micro-form in her child appearances with frustrated playmates and inferable in her adult dealings with friction-points in the U.S.Avengers, follow the same pattern. She will not have the conversation. She will instead take the bad post, cover the bad shift, carry the heavy end of the next job, until the breach has been *worked through* in the literal labor sense. The other party either accepts this restitution or does not; if they require verbal processing, Dani will eventually provide it, but it will be late, clipped, and visibly effortful.

## VII. Intimacy and Dependency

The intimacy ledger is the *single most under-developed register* in the subject's relational repertoire, and it is the most important thing this section can flag for the file.

Dependency, in the helpless sense, has no place in her self-concept. She was raised by a mother whose entire post-trauma identity reconstruction was organized around the refusal of helplessness, and she has inherited Jessica's allergy to being a burden. She will accept help operationally — she is not stupid about the geometry of a fight — but she will not *ask* for help relationally. The ask itself feels, internally, like a category error. This is not pride. It is the absence of a developmental template for the ask.

Intimacy in the full sense — the willingness to be known by another person across registers that do not include shared task — is structurally absent from her canonical record and would, if pursued, require effortful construction rather than instinctive flow. The most plausible developmental path for her, were she to enter a serious dyadic bond, would be a *partner who works alongside her* — someone for whom beat two of the bonding sequence can fire, who can be kin-coded through the normal protocol, and with whom intimacy can then accrete in the spaces between operations. The alternative — the civilian partner, the dyad without operational substrate — is for her a foreign country, navigable only by deliberate effort and likely to feel, to her, slightly unreal.

She is, importantly, *capable of warmth*. The affect is real. What is constrained is not her capacity to feel but her access to a relational *form* in which the feeling can deepen past a certain depth without an external structure holding the relationship in place. The structure her parents had was unceasing crisis. She has inherited the form without yet having found her own version of it, and in the adult timeline the crisis that holds her relationships in place is the standing condition of being Captain America in a broken world.

## VIII. The Relational Template, Repeated

Across every significant bond on record, the same template runs:

1. Encounter under operational conditions.
2. Rapid read; provisional functional trust extended.
3. Stress-tested over time; the person either confirms or declassifies in the silent ledger.
4. If confirmed, kin-coded: invisible promotion to family, expressed only through her willingness to pay disproportionate costs for them.
5. Sustained through *labor* rather than through verbal maintenance.
6. If breached: silent excision, repair only through long accreted presence, conversation last not first.

This template runs with Da Costa's team. It runs with Steve Rogers in *Generations*, where she meets the man whose shield she carries and the meeting is processed operationally rather than reverentially. It runs, most poignantly, with present-day Luke and Jessica when she encounters them as a time-displaced adult: the canonical flatness with which she relates to them is the template's failure mode, because the template has no protocol for *people who are kin by blood but with whom no shared operation has been run in subjective time*. Her parents in the present are, to her template, unprocessable — too important to treat as strangers, too unknown to her current self to treat as kin. She defaults to suppressive composure, which the canon underreports the cost of.

## IX. The Single Diagnostic Relationship

If the file needs one relationship to point at as the diagnostic crux, it is her relationship with the shield itself — and with the implied figure of Steve Rogers, whose mantle she carries without ever having served under him in her original timeline. This is the relationship that exposes the architecture most clearly: she has bonded, in the kin-coding sense, with a *symbol* and a *dead idealized object* rather than a present person. The bond is real, the labor it elicits from her is total, and the structure it provides — the framework of values, the codified protocol for action — substitutes for the dyadic intimacy she has not built with anyone living.

This is the load-bearing relationship of her adult life. Every other bond is downstream of it. The shield is, functionally, her primary attachment figure: present, predictable, holds her, gives her structure, and — critically — *cannot leave*. After a childhood of distributed caregivers who came and went, and a young adulthood (in the displaced timeline) of losing the central caregivers entirely, she has organized her relational life around an object that cannot abandon her. The pathology is mild and the adaptation is high-functioning. But the file should mark, in standing letters, that *the day the shield is taken from her or the role is closed to her, the entire relational architecture loses its keystone*, and the dyadic competencies she has not built will not be there to catch the fall.

She is, in sum, a person who learned to love by watching two damaged people love her well, who learned to trust by watching a roomful of competent strangers keep her alive, who learned to mourn by becoming what the dead had served, and who has not yet learned — has not yet had occasion to learn — how to be loved by one person across an ordinary table on a quiet evening when nothing is on fire. The first four are extraordinary achievements. The fifth is the unwritten chapter, and the file is open on it.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## Preface: The Architecture in One Sentence

Danielle Cage's defensive system is organized around *forward motion through symbolic continuity* — she stays intact by carrying something forward (a mission, a shield, a name, a team), and the entire stack of her defenses, from the most mature down to the few primitive residues that surface under load, is configured to keep that forward motion uninterrupted. Stop her, and the defenses lose their substrate; this is the structural risk that pervades everything below.

The system was built in two phases. **Phase one (childhood, ages 0–~10):** modeled directly on two adult survivors whose own defensive architectures were field-tested and visible — Jessica's blunt-affect suppression, sardonic distance, and pragmatic compartmentalization; Luke's deliberate calm, principled stubbornness, and reframing of indignity into purpose. The child Dani had, in effect, two master classes in mature defense conducted continuously in her sightline, and she absorbed both registers. **Phase two (adolescence and early adulthood, post-loss, in the displaced future):** the parental scaffolding was removed catastrophically, and the defenses she had been *learning* had to become defenses she was *running* — without supervision, under load, in a role (Captain America) that prescribed its own further suite of operational defenses by occupational necessity.

What follows is the full inventory, ranked roughly from most mature (Vaillant's Level IV) downward through neurotic (Level III), immature (Level II), and the small remnant of primitive (Level I) defenses that surface only under extreme conditions.

---

## I. Mature Defenses (Vaillant Level IV) — The Operating Layer

These are the defenses that run in the foreground, visible in every panel of her adult appearances, and they are the reason she presents as high-functioning rather than as a casualty.

### 1. Sublimation — Primary Defense

The dominant mechanism. Grief, rage, survivor's guilt, and the orphan's helplessness are all routed into the work of being Captain America. This is not metaphorical: the shield is the literal containment vessel for affects that have no other safe outlet in her life.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Mission acceptance speed. She does not deliberate visibly when offered work; the acceptance is pre-loaded because the work is psychically necessary, not merely valuable.
- Training intensity disproportionate to her actual physical needs. Her body is super-durable; she does not need to train as hard as she does. The training is affect-management.
- Quality of presence in combat — described across appearances as composed, almost serene under fire. The serenity is the relief of the defense doing its job: while she is fighting, the unprocessed material is metabolized into action.
- Inability to be idle. Documented across her *U.S.Avengers* appearances: she is the one who is already moving while others are still talking.

**Cost:** sublimation requires substrate. When the work is unavailable — peacetime, recovery periods, debrief downtime — the defense starves and the underlying affect surfaces. She has not been shown extensively in such states; the canon avoids the test. Her likely behavior under enforced idleness: ritualized substitutes (drilling, equipment maintenance, perimeter walks) that mimic the sublimative function on a smaller scale.

### 2. Suppression — Continuous Background Defense

Distinct from repression (which is unconscious). Suppression is the deliberate, conscious decision to *set aside* an affect or thought for later, with intention to return. Adult Dani runs suppression on near-constant basis: she registers feelings, acknowledges them privately, parks them, and returns to task.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- The micro-pause before she addresses present-day Jessica or Luke. Not avoidance — a visible, brief, internal placement of the affect somewhere safe before the interaction proceeds.
- Past-tense discussion of her parents that is composed without being detached. This is suppression working correctly: the affect is present, contained, not denied.
- Post-mission affect release that does not occur on-camera but is implied by her ability to start each new appearance "clean." The release is happening somewhere; she is not a flat-affect operator, she is a delayed-affect operator.

**Cost:** suppression is metabolically expensive. The "later" must actually arrive, or the parked material accumulates. Whether she has a place — a person, a ritual, a practice — where the parking lot gets emptied is the central unknown of her clinical picture.

### 3. Anticipation — Operational Defense

She manages future-threat affect by rehearsing the threat in detail rather than avoiding it. This is the defense Steve Rogers ran famously; she inherited it with the shield, but it also tracks her mother's PI-trained pattern-matching.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Pre-mission planning detail; threat-modeling that is granular rather than summary.
- Calm during the actual event because the affect was already metabolized in the rehearsal.
- A tendency to think in scenarios — "if this, then that" — rather than in singular plans.

**Cost:** anticipation can blur into hypervigilance if the threshold for "worth modeling" drops. She is at moderate risk here, given her childhood threat-density training.

### 4. Altruism — Identity-Adjacent Defense

She solves her own pain by attending to others' pain. This is genuine altruism, not reaction-formation; the people she helps are not stand-ins for her, they are the actual point. But the *function* of the altruism is also defensive: it is what makes the unbearable bearable.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Disproportionate attention to civilians-in-frame during combat. She tracks the bystanders even when tactically she could leave them to others.
- The team-as-family treatment of U.S.Avengers personnel within days of joining. This is not naive; it is a defense converting attachment-hunger into operational warmth.
- The instinct to teach, mentor, debrief — channeling her own learning curve outward.

**Cost:** altruism-as-defense can be exploited by anyone who needs help, including those who should not be helped. Her threshold for declining a request is low.

### 5. Humor — Tertiary Mature Defense

Inherited largely from Jessica, modulated by Luke's drier register. Adult Dani uses humor sparingly but well — dry, situationally apt, never at a teammate's expense, occasionally self-deprecating in ways that release tension without distributing it.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Brief verbal release after high-tension sequences.
- Light commentary on the absurdity of her own position (time-displaced super-soldier in a present that contains her dead parents alive) — a humor that is also acknowledgment, the safest form of approach to material she cannot yet handle directly.

**Cost:** minimal. Of all her defenses, humor is the least expensive and the most underused.

---

## II. Neurotic Defenses (Vaillant Level III) — The Middle Layer
