Visible under specific pressures, especially around her family-of-origin material and the role-as-identity fusion.

### 6. Introjective Identification — The Defining Move

She did not merely identify with Steve Rogers; she *introjected* him — took the lost-or-distant object inside, and is now living as a composite self that includes him. Same operation, in a different register, with her parents: she carries them inside, which is part of why she can speak of them composedly. They are not gone; they are inside her, animating decisions.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Phrasing patterns that are not native to her — cadences and word choices that read as Steve's, or as Luke's, surfacing in moments of moral clarity.
- The ritualized care of the shield — cleaning, inspection, placement — that has the quality of tending a relic rather than maintaining equipment.
- A self-concept built forward from inheritance rather than backward from biography.

**Cost:** introjects must be fed by ongoing fidelity to the introjected object's values. If she ever acts in a way that violates Steve's code or her parents' principles, the internal punishment is severe — not guilt in the ordinary sense but a felt sense of *contamination of the inside*. This is a structural vulnerability.

### 7. Intellectualization — Used Around Loss

She discusses her dead parents with operational precision: timelines, circumstances, what was at stake. The detail is real; what is held away is the felt cost. This is not dissociation — she knows the cost — it is intellectualization in its classical form: the substitution of cognitive engagement for affective engagement on material that is too hot for affect.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Past-tense narrative competence about her parents that exceeds her affective availability about them.
- A tendency, when asked about her timeline, to give structural information (what happened, when, why) rather than experiential information (what it was like).
- Strategic framing of her own life events — her arrival in the present is "an opportunity for cross-temporal operational learning," not "I get to see my mom again."

**Cost:** the material remains undigested. Intellectualization preserves the data while sequestering the meaning.

### 8. Reaction Formation — Minor, Specific

Not a major defense but visible in one place: her warmth toward present-day Luke and Jessica is calibrated *down*, not up. The grief-pressure to cling to them is so high that the defense produces a slightly excessive professionalism — she is more correct, more distant, more "Captain" with them than with strangers. This is reaction formation: the impulse is reversed at the surface.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Use of formal address or military-style courtesy with parents who, in her timeline, called her by her childhood name.
- Avoidance of physical contact that exceeds operational necessity.
- A trained smile that briefly precedes any extended interaction with them.

**Cost:** the parents register the distance as rejection or as ordinary time-displacement awkwardness; the actual cost to her is the daily expenditure of holding the impulse in reverse.

### 9. Isolation of Affect — Field-Operational

Closely related to intellectualization but more granular: the ability to handle, in real time, a fact whose affect would impair the mission. Standard for senior operators; she runs it well.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Reporting a teammate injury during ongoing engagement with no voice-change.
- Continuing engagement after sustaining a hit that would, with affect attached, demand pause.
- Post-action affect surfacing that confirms the affect was present, just sequestered.

**Cost:** affect that is reliably isolated in the field must be reliably reintegrated out of it. If reintegration is skipped, the isolated material becomes the substrate for later somatization or sudden affect-floods.

### 10. Displacement — Channeled, Productive

Anger at the universe for taking her parents → effective application of force against actual enemies. Grief about her timeline → care for present-day teammates. These are not pure mature defenses because the original target is being substituted, not transformed; but the substitution is consistently in pro-social directions.

**Behavioral signatures:**
- Combat intensity that occasionally exceeds tactical necessity by a small margin — the extra ten percent that says some of this is for something else.
- Protective behavior toward younger teammates that has a maternal-substitute quality.

**Cost:** displacement requires acceptable targets. If targets are scarce, the affect routes inward (self-criticism, somatization) or finds inappropriate targets (subordinates, allies).

---

## III. Immature Defenses (Vaillant Level II) — The Stress Layer

Rare in baseline, present under specific load conditions. Their relative absence is what marks her as high-functioning; their occasional presence is what marks her as human.

### 11. Somatization — Latent, Probable

Her body does not break to ordinary force. This means somatic distress, when it occurs, must take subtler forms: sleep disruption, appetite shifts, withdrawal from non-mission contact, the quiet inflammation of a body that is processing something the mind has parked. The canon does not show this on-camera; the clinical inference is that it is occurring off-camera.

**Predicted behavioral signatures:**
- Reduced sleep windows in periods between missions (the down-time when suppressed material surfaces).
- A pattern of "training through" minor systemic discomfort that would, in a less durable operator, prompt rest.
- Migrainoid or tension symptoms in periods of forced contact with present-day parents.

### 12. Passive Aggression — Trace, Inherited

She inherited Jessica's capacity for it but does not generally deploy it. Trace appearances: a particular brand of bureaucratic compliance — doing exactly what is asked, no more, no less — when asked to do something she disagrees with by authority she cannot openly defy. This is the lowest-grade form of the defense and is, in her case, almost a parody of it; she signals her objection by the precision of her compliance.

### 13. Acting Out — Effectively Suppressed

Notable for its near-absence. A subject with her exposure profile and loss history could plausibly act out in any number of registers (sexual, substance, recklessness). She does not. The suppression is so complete that it warrants flagging: defenses this clean often indicate either genuine integration or successful redirection. In her case it is largely the former (the sublimation is doing the work) but the *completeness* is suspicious enough to be worth monitoring.

### 14. Fantasy — Minimal, Specific

She does not appear to retreat into fantasy as a general mechanism. The exception: a probable, unwitnessed pattern of imagining alternative timelines in which her parents survived. This is not pathological fantasy (immersive, identity-displacing); it is more like brief intrusive counterfactuals that she allows briefly and then dismisses. The dismissal is itself a defensive operation.

---

## IV. Primitive Defenses (Vaillant Level I) — The Floor

Largely absent. Their absence is the clearest evidence that her early attachment was, in fact, secure — primitive defenses are the floor a person retreats to when nothing else works, and she has not been shown there.

### 15. Denial — Not Present in Material Form

She does not deny her parents are dead. She does not deny the difficulty of her position. She does not deny her own affect, only parks it. This is a major clinical positive.

### 16. Splitting — Not Present

No evidence of all-good/all-bad object representations. She holds nuanced views of allies, enemies, institutions, and herself. She can criticize Steve Rogers' tradition while carrying his shield; she can love her mother while seeing her flaws; she can work within a flawed institution without idealizing or devaluing it.

### 17. Projective Identification — Not Present

No evidence of inducing in others affects she cannot own. She does not, for instance, make her teammates carry her grief by inducing protective worry; she does not make enemies carry her rage by provoking them past tactical need.

### 18. Dissociation — Trace Only, Under Extreme Load

The flatness around present-day Luke and Jessica is, in part, a controlled dissociative operation — a small, time-limited compartmentalization to make the encounter survivable. This is the only primitive defense with measurable on-screen presence, and it is deployed narrowly and (for now) sustainably.

---

## V. Compensatory Mechanisms — The Positive Side of the Ledger

Distinct from defenses (which manage affect) — compensations are the *structures she has built* that supply what was lost or what was never available.

### Positive Compensations

1. **The Role as Container.** Captain America is not a job; it is a *holding environment* in Winnicott's sense. The role tells her what to do, what to value, how to comport herself, when to act and when to wait. It contains the orphan by giving the orphan a function.

2. **The Team as Chosen Family.** U.S.Avengers and equivalents replace, structurally, the family-of-origin. The replacement is not denial of the original (she does not pretend the team is her parents); it is substitution at the level of *function*: who I check in with, who I worry about, who worries about me.

3. **The Shield as Transitional Object.** In the developmental sense — an object that bridges the lost relationship and the present self. She tends it ritually; it is the daily site of contact with the introjected ideal.

4. **The Symbol as Trans-personal Identity.** Identifying with Captain America as a *tradition* (not just a person) gives her access to a self larger than her biography. She is the latest of many; her grief is one of many griefs the role has carried. This is a powerful and stabilizing compensation.

5. **Inherited Code as Decisional Shortcut.** Her parents' values, internalized, give her a fast-acting ethical compass that reduces decisional load under pressure. She does not need to derive ethics from scratch; she runs theirs and Steve's.

### Negative / Risky Compensations

1. **Role-Identity Fusion.** The role contains her; she is also *contained by* it. Loss of the role (forced retirement, shield loss, public discredit) would be experienced as loss of self, not loss of job.

2. **Mission-Dependence for Affect Regulation.** She regulates by doing. Without a mission, the regulation system runs idle and the parked affects surface. Peacetime is her unaddressed vulnerability.

3. **Team-Family Conflation.** Treating teammates as kin means a teammate's death is a family death. Her introjective grief solution has been stress-tested for parents-already-dead; it has not been tested for a chosen-family loss under her command.

4. **Avoidance-by-Distance with Living Parents.** Compensation for the impossible affect of seeing her dead parents alive — calibrated reaction-formation distance — also means she does not get the repair the encounter could, in principle, offer. The defense protects function at the cost of integration.

5. **Hyperresponsibility as Self-Concept.** The Atlas pattern is, simultaneously, the engine of her competence and the structural reason she cannot rest. Compensated for now by the durability of her body and the abundance of her purpose; uncompensated if either fails.

---

## VI. Summary Read

The defensive architecture is **mature-dominant, neurotic-supplemented, immature-trace, primitive-near-absent** — a profile consistent with a securely-attached operator under chronic high load. The system is not pathological; it is expensive. The expense is paid by ongoing access to mission, team, and role. Remove any of those three substrates and the stack begins to lose footing, starting with sublimation (which starves), proceeding through suppression (whose parking lot fills), and exposing the unprocessed grief at the base.

Her defenses are not what is wrong with her. They are what is *holding* her, and they are holding her well. The clinical question is not whether the architecture works — it works — but whether anyone in her life is positioned to be there when, eventually, it needs to be set down for maintenance. On current evidence, she has not yet identified that person, that practice, or that place. Until she does, the system runs hot, beautifully, and alone.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: DANIELLE CAGE

*Decadal clinical mapping across the bifurcated developmental record — infancy through the adult Captain America phase of the displaced 20XX timeline. Frameworks deployed: Bowlby/Ainsworth attachment; Mahler separation-individuation; Erikson psychosocial stages; Vaillant's defense hierarchy; Stern's affective attunement; Linehan's emotion-regulation construct; Janoff-Bulman's assumptive-world theory; Bonanno's resilience trajectory model; Neimeyer's meaning-reconstruction grief theory.*

---

## DECADE ONE: INFANCY THROUGH LATE CHILDHOOD (Age 0 – ~10)

### Sub-period 1A: Natal through 18 months (Bendis *Pulse* / *New Avengers* baseline)

**Affect regulation.** Pre-verbal, dyadically scaffolded. The infant's regulatory apparatus is the caregiver's nervous system — Stern's "affect attunement" being the live mechanism. Two observations from canon constrain the read: (a) Jessica Jones-Cage carries the baby into combat-adjacent zones repeatedly, and (b) Luke Cage is the demonstrably calmer of the two parental nervous systems — recurrent panel-level data shows him doing the soothing, the swaying, the holding-while-Jessica-paces. The infant's primary co-regulator is therefore the father, with the mother providing high-vigilance environmental scanning. This produces, at the level of autonomic conditioning, a child whose baseline arousal is *calibrated to her father's slow heart rate while she is held by him* — a somatic anchor that will recur as a self-soothing template for decades.

**Cognitive style (proto).** Object permanence is acquired in an environment where caregivers literally vanish — sometimes for missions, sometimes through more disturbing mechanisms (the Jarvis-Skrull abduction during *Secret Invasion* being the canonical worst case). The internal working model that consolidates is *people you trust are sometimes not the people they appear to be, and sometimes are gone before you understand they have left*. This is not consciously held by an 18-month-old; it is encoded in the limbic substrate as a low-grade prior that disconfirmation must be active rather than assumed.

**Self-concept (proto).** Mirror-stage data unavailable. What the canon does show is that she is *named and held by many*: Squirrel Girl, Jarvis, Jessica Drew, Wolverine, Iron Fist all hold, address, and orient to her. The Mahlerian symbiotic phase is unusually distributed; the infant's first sense of "me" forms in a field of multiple reliable holders rather than a single dyadic mirror. This is not pathological — kibbutz and extended-family data support that distributed early caregiving, when consistent, produces secure attachment with a *generalized* rather than maternally-concentrated trust template.

### Sub-period 1B: Toddlerhood and early childhood (Walker-era *Power Man and Iron Fist* / *Jessica Jones* 2016)

**Affect regulation.** Early verbalization shows precocity — she is depicted as articulate and composed in scenes that would dysregulate a typical toddler (strangers in the apartment, parental shouting, weapons within sight). This is consistent with what attachment researchers call *parentified composure* in observationally-developed children of high-affect parents: the child learns to model emotional steadiness as a contribution to family equilibrium. Critically, this is not yet a defense — at this age it is mimetic, an imitation of the parent (Luke) whose regulation works. Whether it ossifies into a true defense depends on whether the child is permitted to dysregulate when she needs to. The available canon is ambiguous; Jessica's mothering style is loving but blunt, and she is not always the parent who tolerates a tantrum well. Luke is. The likely pattern: Dani routes affect-discharge toward her father and self-regulation toward her mother, learning both modes by attribution.

**Cognitive style.** Erikson's *autonomy vs. shame* and *initiative vs. guilt* stages unfold inside a household where adult autonomy is constantly performed and constantly costly. Modeled message: *you can do anything, and you will pay for everything you do*. The child's emerging cognitive style is *consequentialist early* — she observes that her parents weigh actions in terms of who gets hurt, not who is right, and the pattern is laid down. This is the seed of the adult's *people-centric* rather than *principle-centric* moral cognition.

**Self-concept.** "I am the reason." Both parents repeatedly invoke her — in her hearing — as the reason for and against various decisions. A child who is the *recurrent stated motive* for adult action develops an early, weighty sense of mattering. In healthy form: high self-worth. In shadow form: the seed of the hyperresponsibility pattern visible in adulthood. Both are seeded simultaneously and will not separate.

### Sub-period 1C: Middle childhood (extrapolated — limited canon)

**Affect regulation.** Suppression begins to emerge as a deliberate strategy rather than an imitation. The child whose parents are routinely in mortal danger learns not to add to their load — a documented pattern in children of first responders, military families, and (the closest analog) children of vigilantes. The likely behavioral signature: bringing distress to parents only when it cannot be self-managed, and self-managing increasingly young. This is Vaillant *suppression* — a mature defense — appearing prematurely. Premature mature defenses are double-edged: they buy functioning at the cost of the developmental practice of being unregulated and surviving it.

**Cognitive style.** Pattern-matching as inherited cognitive style emerges. Jessica's PI cognition (read the room, distrust the surface, find the lie) is the ambient water; the child absorbs it. By middle childhood she is, almost certainly, the kid who notices when adults are lying to her and does not say so. This is a competence with a cost — it forecloses the developmental experience of *being protectively deceived and benefiting from it* (Santa, monsters-under-the-bed reassurances, the small fictions that scaffold a child's sense of a managed world).

**Self-concept.** Consolidating around *inheritor*. The household contains, visibly, the artifacts and visitors of two superhero careers. Identity formation in middle childhood normally involves trying on roles; this child's available roles are *be like Mom, be like Dad, or be the civilian who watches them leave*. The third option is, structurally, the rejection of the family. The first two are continuations. The choice is functionally pre-made by environment.

---

## DECADE TWO: ADOLESCENCE (Age ~10 – ~20)

*Canon goes dark here for child-Dani; the adult-Dani backstory implies but does not detail this period. The following is reconstructed from the bracketing data: the secure-vigilant child of Decade One, the composed-orphan operator of Decade Three.*

**Affect regulation.** This is the decade in which the somatic inheritance begins to assert itself. If powers manifest at puberty (the modal pattern for Marvel inherited abilities), the adolescent suddenly inhabits a body that does not break. The interoceptive feedback loop that signals to a normal teenager *you are scared, your hands are shaking, retreat* is muted by a body that does not shake under threats it could survive. Affect regulation must therefore be *cognitively constructed* rather than *somatically given* — she has to *decide* to be afraid, in some sense, because her body will not insist. This is the developmental hinge for what becomes, in the adult, the eerily controlled affect. It is not dissociation; it is the absence of one of the autonomic brakes that normally constrains adolescent reactivity. She must build, by adolescent effort, the brake her body does not supply.

**Cognitive style.** Erikson's *identity vs. role confusion*. The available identity options — given parentage, powers, and environment — are narrow and weighty. Healthy adolescent identity formation requires a *moratorium* (Marcia) in which the adolescent tries on identities that are not the family's. Whether Dani was permitted such a moratorium is unknown; the timeline implies the parents die before she completes one. If so, she enters adulthood with a *foreclosed* identity (Marcia's foreclosure status: commitment without exploration) — the role chosen, by default of context, without the developmental work of having considered and rejected alternatives. This is consistent with the adult's striking lack of role-ambivalence. She does not wonder if she should be doing something else. Foreclosed identities are highly stable until the foreclosure is challenged from outside; this is a latent vulnerability of adult-Dani's psyche.

**Self-concept.** The adolescent self-concept almost certainly cycles through *daughter* and *heir* and arrives, at the precipitating event of her parents' loss, on *successor*. The succession is to *Steve Rogers*, not to *Luke Cage* — a substitution worth pausing on. To take her father's mantle would be to compete with him in absentia, to declare herself his replacement, to enact an Oedipal completion her psyche likely cannot tolerate. To take Captain America's shield is to step laterally — into a symbol that is honored *by* her father rather than embodied *as* her father. It is the only succession available that does not require her to symbolically supplant the parent she lost. This is, in object-relations terms, an elegantly defended choice.

**Defenses (consolidating).** Sublimation comes online as the organizing mature defense. The grief of orphanhood is channeled into mission rather than discharged through mourning. Anticipation (planning for the worst, structuring for survival) becomes habitual. Suppression — already present from middle childhood — deepens. Notably *not* consolidating: any of the primitive defenses (splitting, projective identification, primitive denial) that would be expected in a child who lost both parents traumatically without secure earlier attachment. The early foundation holds; the late catastrophe is processed through mature machinery. This is what Bonanno calls the *resilient trajectory* — distinct from recovery (which involves a depressive trough followed by return to baseline). Resilient subjects do not trough; they integrate. The cost of resilience is the absence of the depressive trough's processing work. Material that would have been worked through in a trough remains, instead, encysted.

---

## DECADE THREE: EARLY ADULTHOOD AS CAPTAIN AMERICA OF 20XX (Age ~20 – ~30)

### Pre-displacement: the home timeline

**Affect regulation.** Operational-grade. The cognitive-constructive regulation built in adolescence is now mature. She runs hot under control: capable of warmth, humor, tenderness, and rapid escalation to lethal competence, with clean transitions between registers. The Linehan model of emotion regulation — observe, describe, participate, non-judgmentally, one-mindfully, effectively — describes her operational style as if written for her. This is not coincidence; it is the convergent endpoint of a developmental trajectory that selected for it.

**Cognitive style.** Decisive, low-rumination, ethically pre-committed. She does not deliberate during action; the deliberation has happened upstream, in the construction of her operating principles. Under fire she executes; after action she does not relitigate. This is partially Luke's inheritance (the man who decides and stays decided) and partially Jessica's (the operator who has already paid for indecision and will not pay again). It is also, clinically, a known feature of foreclosed identity: the work of deciding is done, so action is fast.

**Self-concept.** *Inheritor of the principle.* Stable, integrated, ego-syntonic. She is Captain America the way her father was Power Man — the name is not a costume, it is a load-bearing element of self. Threats to the role would be experienced as threats to self; this is the latent fragility of an otherwise enviably integrated identity.

### Post-displacement: the present-day timeline (U.S.Avengers era)

This is the most clinically interesting phase of the longitudinal record because it places the subject in proximity to her *living* parents — people she has buried in her own timeline — and the canon understates the resulting affective load.

**Affect regulation.** Holds — visibly, deliberately, with the slight over-control that suggests effort. The clinical reading: she is *suppressing* (mature defense) rather than *dissociating* (primitive). The difference is observable in whether the suppressed material is accessible when she chooses to access it. The canon does not give us a scene where she chooses to access it, which is itself the datum. The suppression is *unbroken* — admirable as performance, concerning as a clinical sign that the material has not been integrated.

**Cognitive style.** Compartmentalization in the technical sense — not as a pathology but as a deliberately constructed cognitive partition. *Present-day Luke and Jessica are not my parents; my parents are dead. These are alternate-timeline persons who happen to share faces and names. I will treat them with appropriate respect and operational courtesy and not as kin.* This is an extraordinarily demanding cognitive act sustained continuously. It works. It is also exactly the structure that, if it failed, would fail catastrophically — compartments do not leak; they rupture.

**Self-concept.** Here is the most fragile zone. To be *the daughter* in the present timeline would be to undo *the inheritor* of her own. The two selves cannot coexist; one negates the other. She has chosen, presumably without naming the choice, to remain the inheritor — to keep her dead parents dead in her self-construction rather than to retroactively un-orphan herself via the living-but-other versions present. This is a defensible choice and possibly the only sustainable one, but it requires her to *refuse* a form of reparation that is, uniquely, available to her and to almost no other grieving subject in history. The cost of that refusal is not visible in canon and is therefore unprocessed.

**Janoff-Bulman assumptive-world analysis.** The three core assumptions Janoff-Bulman identifies as shattered by trauma — *the world is benevolent, the world is meaningful, the self is worthy* — show, in adult-Dani, a specific reconstruction profile: (1) the world is *not* assumed benevolent; it is assumed to *require* benevolent actors, which is a different and more durable structure; (2) meaning is *constructed through mission* rather than discovered in the world; (3) self-worth is *earned through embodiment of the role*, not given. This is a fully-reconstructed assumptive world, not a shattered one. The reconstruction is competent. The reconstruction is also load-bearing in a way the pre-trauma assumptive world would not have needed to be — remove the mission, and the worth-construction loses its scaffold.

**Neimeyer meaning-reconstruction.** She has successfully completed what Neimeyer calls the *narrative reconstruction* of bereavement — the dead parents are integrated into a coherent life-story that gives their deaths meaning (they died for the world she now defends). What has not been demonstrated in canon is the *relational reconstruction* — the renegotiation of the ongoing internal relationship with the lost figures. Adult-Dani speaks *of* her parents; she is not shown speaking *to* them, internally or ritually. The internal-relational work of grief is the slowest and least visible work, and there is no canonical evidence she has done it. The proximity of their living counterparts in the present-day timeline is, clinically, an *intervention opportunity* she is structurally barred from accepting.

---

## CROSS-DECADAL SYNTHESIS

**The affect-regulation trajectory** runs: dyadic co-regulation (infancy) → mimetic composure (toddlerhood) → premature suppression (middle childhood) → cognitive-constructive regulation (adolescence, forced by somatic muting) → operational-grade controlled-warmth (adulthood). Each stage's adaptation became the next stage's substrate. The endpoint is enviable competence with a single structural absence: she has never, in the available record, been *unregulated and survived it with witnesses*. The developmental experience of catastrophic affect being held by another and proving non-destructive — which is the deep substrate of adult emotional intimacy — is the one experience her history did not provide. Her parents, busy surviving, could not provide it; her teammates, organized around mission, do not invite it.

**The cognitive-style trajectory** runs: distributed-trust prior (infancy) → consequentialist moral cognition (early childhood) → inherited pattern-matching vigilance (middle childhood) → foreclosed identity commitment (adolescence) → decisive low-rumination execution (adulthood). Each stage narrowed the cognitive aperture in the direction of action-readiness. The endpoint is a mind beautifully shaped for the role she occupies and poorly equipped for the role she does not occupy — peacetime, retirement, intimacy without mission-frame, the work of being a person rather than a function.

**The self-concept trajectory** runs: the-reason (early childhood) → the-inheritor (middle childhood and adolescence) → the-successor (the precipitating loss) → the-symbol (adult operational identity). Each stage is a defensible integration of the prior; none required revision of the foundation. This is unusually clean — most subjects' self-concept trajectories include at least one decade of repudiation, the adolescent or young-adult moratorium in which the inherited self is rejected before being, often, partially reclaimed. She does not appear to have had this. Her self is continuous with her infancy in a way most adults' selves are not. This is the deep source of her stability and the deep source of her fragility: a self that has never been broken and reassembled has never demonstrated to itself that it can survive being broken.

**The defense-organization trajectory** runs: distributed reliance (infancy) → imitative composure (toddlerhood) → premature suppression (middle childhood) → sublimation and anticipation come online (adolescence under loss) → mature defenses fully consolidated, primitive defenses notably absent (adulthood). The Vaillant hierarchy reads as textbook mature throughout, with the caveat that the maturity arrived earlier than developmentally normative and was, in a sense, *forced* by environment rather than *grown* through the normal sequence of regression and repair. Forced maturity holds well; it has not, in her case, been tested by conditions that would normally regress an adult to primitive defenses (the prolonged immobilization of grief, the helplessness of being cared for through illness, the powerlessness of watching a loved one die slowly). The defenses are mature. They have not been stress-tested across the full range a long life will eventually present.

**The single longitudinal thesis.** Across every decade, the same developmental logic recurs: *environment requires of her a competence beyond her stage, and she meets the requirement; the meeting is real and load-bearing; the cost is the absence of the developmental experience the requirement skipped over.* She is a person constructed entirely of competent adaptations to conditions that demanded them. There is no part of her that is purely *given* — no zone of unearned ease, no untested certainty, no foundation laid in safety she did not have to manufacture. This is the strength of her and the loneliness of her, and the two are the same fact viewed from inside and outside.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Subject: Danielle Cage (child-record + adult-record, integrated longitudinal)

---

## 0. Framing & Methodological Notes

This is a two-record evaluation of one person. The childhood file (infancy through approximately age six as documented in *The Pulse* #13 onward, *New Avengers*, *Avengers: The Initiative*, *Power Man and Iron Fist*, and *Jessica Jones* vol. 2) gives us developmental data: caregiving environment, regulatory milestones, exposure profile. The adult file (the displaced-future Captain America of 20XX from *Avengers* #38 forward, *U.S.Avengers*, *Generations: The Americas*) gives us outcome data: functional level, defensive organization, symptom load. The two are continuous in a non-trivial sense — the adult is *this* child raised in *that* household and then catastrophically bereaved between the two records. Diagnostic statements that hold across both records get more weight than those that hold only at one endpoint.

The assessment uses DSM-5-TR criteria with ICD-11 cross-walks where the latter captures the picture better (notably for adjustment, complex trauma, and prolonged grief, where ICD-11 is more behaviorally precise). Where the differential turns on phenomena outside DSM (resilience phenotype, hyperresponsibility, identity-fused role pathology), I name the construct, cite the literature lineage, and reason from observable behavior rather than from labels.

**Bottom-line up front:** No current Axis-I disorder meeting threshold. Subclinical features in three domains (hyperresponsibility, suppressed grief, role-fused identity). Risk profile is *latent and conditional* — she is well now under conditions that demand her function; the diagnostic risk lights up if those conditions are removed.

---

## 1. Mental Status (Adult Record, Composite Across Appearances)

**Appearance / Behavior.** Tall, athletic, posture squared and weight-centered — the standing posture of someone trained to deliver or absorb impact without telegraph. Grooming utilitarian; the uniform is the wardrobe. Eye contact direct, sustained, modulated (not the unblinking lock of dominance display, not the glance-and-drop of social anxiety — the calibrated gaze of an operator reading a room). Psychomotor activity within normal limits; no tics, no agitation, no retardation. Hands at rest hands. She is comfortable in stillness — a clinically relevant detail, since most operators of her exposure profile cannot sit without micro-fidgeting.

**Speech.** Rate normal, volume modulated, prosody intact and warm when warmth is offered. Vocabulary is operational-precise rather than ornate. She speaks in complete sentences and does not trail. Under stress, sentences shorten and verbs front-load — a sign of cognitive economy, not of dysregulation.

**Mood / Affect.** Stated mood when offered: "Fine," "Working," "Good to be here." Observed affect: euthymic baseline, narrow but not flat range, congruent with content, mobilizes appropriately to warmth and humor. Affect does not blunt under threat; it *compresses* — the distinction matters. A blunted affect would mean the emotional signal is absent; a compressed affect means the bandwidth of expression narrows while the signal continues to drive behavior accurately.

**Thought process.** Linear, goal-directed, no loosening, no flight, no blocking. Pattern-matching speed is high — Jessica's investigative inheritance.

**Thought content.** No delusions, no ideation, no obsessions or compulsions on record. No persecutory framing despite a biographical history that would license it. Notably *absent*: rumination. She does not relitigate.

**Perception.** No hallucinations, no derealization on record. The time-displacement situation invites a derealization differential (see §5) which the canon does not engage but a real workup would screen for.

**Cognition.** Oriented x4. Attention, concentration, working memory all consistent with high-level operational performance. No documented memory complaints.

**Insight / Judgment.** Insight is *operational* (excellent regarding mission and team) and *partial* regarding her own inner life (the cost-side ledger appears not to be open to her). Judgment is consistently high under acute conditions; chronic-condition judgment (about her own pacing, her own need for rest, her own grief work) is untested.

**Suicidality / Homicidality.** None on record, no indicators present. Lethality of person is high (occupational), lethality of intent is null.

---

## 2. Etiological Formulation

Three layered etiological strata produced the current presentation.

**Stratum I — Constitutional.** Genetic inheritance includes a nervous system riding on a body that does not break (see Medical). This is not psychiatrically neutral. Subdermal durability and accelerated healing mute the interoceptive pain-anticipation signal that, in baseline humans, brakes approach behavior toward threat. The neurological consequence over a developmental arc is a *recalibrated threat-appraisal baseline*: stimuli that would register as "danger, retreat" in a normal nervous system register as "stimulus, assess" in hers. This is not fearlessness; it is a different fear gradient. Clinically it predicts low panic-disorder risk, low somatic-anxiety risk, and an elevated risk of *under-detection* of internal distress (because the body's distress channel is partially closed).

**Stratum II — Developmental.** Two competent, demonstrative parents present and prioritizing across the documented child years; this is the foundation that holds. Layered on top: a chaotically rotating secondary caregiving network (Squirrel Girl, Jarvis, Avengers personnel, Iron Fist, Wolverine, Jessica Drew) and a parental dyad that periodically and unpredictably vanished into combat for hours to days. The internal working model laid down in this configuration is *primary love is reliable; primary presence is not; safety is distributed*. Three specific perinatal/early-childhood events warrant naming as discrete etiological loadings: (a) the Skrull-Jarvis abduction during *Secret Invasion*, (b) the *Siege*-era debates about evacuation, which the child would have registered as ambient parental fear-state without understanding content, (c) the *Jessica Jones* (2016) faked-separation cover, where the child was a piece in adult tradecraft. None of these is a discrete trauma in the Criterion-A sense; cumulatively they constitute the *texture* of her infancy, which is the etiologically relevant variable.

**Stratum III — Catastrophic adult loss.** Between the child record and the adult record, in the displaced future timeline, both parents die or are otherwise lost, and Steve Rogers dies or retires. She inherits the shield in that vacancy. This is the precipitating event-cluster for the adult presentation. It is the variable that converts a developmentally interesting child into a diagnostically interesting adult. The form her grief took — sublimation into role, identification with the lost idealized object — is the central etiological fact of her adult psychiatric picture.

The integration: a constitutionally damped interoceptive signal + a securely-attached but distributed early model + a catastrophic mid-life loss resolved by introjective identification with a symbol = a high-functioning adult whose competence is real, whose pain channel is half-closed at the neurological level and half-closed at the defensive level, and whose role-as-identity is doing the structural work that grief work would do in a person whose nervous system could afford to feel it.

---

## 3. Diagnostic Considerations — Endorsed, Subclinical, or Conditional

### 3.1 Subclinical Hyperresponsibility Pattern (no DSM code; closest analog: OCPD-spectrum traits without disorder threshold)

*Endorsed at subclinical, ego-syntonic level.*

**Presentation.** Difficulty declining mission, difficulty resting, identity fusion with role, internal moral ledger that runs continuously, scrupulosity about being *worthy of* inherited symbols (shield, parents, name). The pattern is not OCPD proper — there is no rigidity, no perfectionism that impedes task completion, no hoarding, no preoccupation with rules over outcomes, no interpersonal cost from inflexibility. What is shared with the OCPD construct is the duty-saturated internal world and the inability to experience leisure as legitimate.

**Behavioral markers in canon.** She steps onto the U.S.Avengers team and is operational within hours. She does not appear to take liberty. She does not discuss recreational interests, hobbies, off-duty preferences. The absence is the data. When asked about her parents, she answers operationally and moves on — the move-on is the symptom.

**Etiology.** Modeled directly off two parents whose lives demonstrated, in vivo, that the work does not stop and that love is a thing you do while doing the work. Reinforced by the catastrophic loss: rest, in her formative adult experience, was the condition under which her parents were vulnerable. Action is, at a procedural-memory level, the safer state.

**Course.** Stable, ego-syntonic, currently adaptive. Becomes a diagnosis-worthy concern only on context-change.

### 3.2 Suppressed / Under-Stress-Tested Grief Integration (no current PGD; ICD-11 Prolonged Grief Disorder ruled out, see §4)

*Endorsed as a clinically significant suppressed-defense configuration, not a disorder.*

**Presentation.** Composed past-tense reference to dead parents. No avoidance of their memory, no intrusion, no longing-with-impairment, no identity-disruption *attributable to the grief*. The identity-disruption present (role-fusion) is a *solution* to the grief, not a symptom of unresolved grief. The grief is *contained*, not absent and not pathologically prolonged.

**The diagnostic subtlety.** Suppression (Vaillant mature-defense) and avoidance (immature defense / PGD symptom) look identical at the surface and differ at the cost-line. Suppression is the conscious choice to set aside affect to function, with the affect available when the operator chooses to access it. Avoidance is the unconscious blockade of affect such that access produces decompensation. The canon does not show her testing the seam, so the differential cannot be settled from the existing record. *Working assumption based on her overall mature defensive profile*: suppression, not avoidance. *Caveat held open*: the consistency of her composure across conditions that would crack most operators is at the upper edge of plausible for pure suppression, and a partial avoidant overlay cannot be excluded.

### 3.3 Role-Fused Identity (no DSM code; closest analog: identity-foreclosure in Marcia's framework, with introjective character organization)

*Endorsed and clinically central.*

**Presentation.** "I am Captain America" is operating closer to "Captain America is what I am" than to "Captain America is what I do." The shield is ego-structure. Threats to the role would be more destabilizing than threats to her life — a clinically observable inversion that defines the configuration.

**Why not a Personality Disorder.** Identity foreclosure is not pathological per se. It becomes a personality-disorder candidate only when it produces interpersonal dysfunction, affective dysregulation, or impaired reality testing. None of these are present. Her interpersonal pattern is warm and functional, her affect is regulated, her reality testing is intact. She has *narrowed* her identity to a load-bearing form, not *fragmented* it.

**Where the risk sits.** If the role is removed (forced retirement, loss of shield, return to her own timeline with the role obsolete, peacetime), the identity scaffolding does the work it was built to do and the underlying grief is exposed in an unintegrated state. This is the high-probability decompensation pathway. It is the pathway every clinical record on her should flag for any handler contemplating reassignment, demobilization, or repatriation.

### 3.4 Adjustment-Related Features Around Time-Displacement

*Subclinical, partially endorsed, under-engaged in canon.*

**Presentation.** She is living in a present that contains the living bodies of the parents she has buried. The clinical literature on this exact situation is, for obvious reasons, thin — but the closest analogs (adults reuniting with believed-dead family, witnesses to "doubles," dissociative-identity adjacent encounters with one's own past) predict significant affective load. Her observed affect with present-day Luke and Jessica is *flatter than baseline* — and her baseline is already controlled. This is either (a) superb suppression in service of not contaminating the present-timeline relationship with her grief, which would be ethically and clinically sophisticated, or (b) avoidant compartmentalization, which would be fragile. Without longitudinal data on the relationship, the differential is not resolvable.

The diagnostic point: this *should* register, in any honest workup, as an under-investigated zone. The canon's silence on it is not evidence of its absence.

---

## 4. Differential — What She Is Not, and Why

This is the rigorous half of the workup. The exposure profile invites a long differential; nearly all of it is ruled out, and the reasons matter.

### 4.1 Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.81 / ICD-11 6B40) — **Ruled out.**

Criterion A is met many times over (combat exposure, parental death, civilizational threat). Criteria B–E are not.

- **B (Intrusion):** No documented flashbacks, nightmares, intrusive memories, or physiological reactivity to cues. Her sleep is not on record but her daytime functioning is not interrupted by intrusion phenomena.
- **C (Avoidance):** She does not avoid trauma reminders. She wears Steve Rogers' shield daily — the central reminder of an entire era of loss. She works with the present-day Avengers, who are reminders of her dead world. She does not avoid; she engages.
- **D (Negative cognitions / mood):** Absent. Worldview is not persistently negative, self-blame is not present, anhedonia is not present, detachment is selective (mission-appropriate) rather than pervasive.
- **E (Arousal / reactivity):** No hypervigilance beyond occupational norm, no exaggerated startle (her startle is *low*, consistent with subdermal durability), no irritability, no recklessness, no sleep disturbance on record, no concentration impairment.

The PTSD picture is absent. The most parsimonious explanation is a *resilience phenotype* in the technical sense (Bonanno 2004): the empirically established outcome trajectory in which roughly one-third to one-half of trauma-exposed individuals maintain stable functioning without symptomatic disorder, attributable to a combination of secure attachment substrate, hardiness, positive emotionality, and access to coping resources. She fits the resilience trajectory squarely. Subthreshold trauma sequelae are likely present (some affective narrowing, the suppressed-grief configuration) but do not aggregate to disorder.

### 4.2 Complex PTSD (ICD-11 6B41) — **Ruled out.**

Requires the PTSD criteria *plus* disturbances in self-organization: affective dysregulation, negative self-concept, interpersonal disturbance. None of these are present. Her self-concept is positive and stable, her affect is regulated, her interpersonal pattern is warm and functional. CPTSD is the wrong frame.

### 4.3 Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.89 / ICD-11 6B42) — **Ruled out.**

PGD requires intense yearning or preoccupation with the deceased *plus* at least three symptoms (identity disruption, marked sense of disbelief, avoidance of reminders, intense emotional pain, difficulty reintegrating, emotional numbness, meaninglessness, loneliness) producing clinically significant impairment, twelve months post-loss minimum.

She does not present with yearning-preoccupation. The identity disruption present is a *resolution* of grief through identification, not an unresolved-grief symptom. She does not avoid reminders, she does not show meaninglessness, she is not impaired. The grief has integrated through an introjective pathway that is non-normative but not pathological.

The distinction to hold: *integration through identification* (mature, costly, available to her because her ego organization could support it) versus *failure to integrate* (PGD). She is in the first category. The cost of the first category is the role-fusion described in §3.3, not a grief disorder.

### 4.4 Major Depressive Disorder (DSM-5-TR 296.2x/296.3x) — **Ruled out.**

No depressed mood reported or observed, no anhedonia, no neurovegetative signs on record, no worthlessness, no impaired concentration, no SI. The composed affect is not depressive flatness — it is operationally narrow affect with intact range when context invites it. She laughs. She connects. The depressive picture is not present.

### 4.5 Persistent Depressive Disorder / Dysthymia — **Ruled out.** No chronic low mood signature, no two-year history of depressive features. Her baseline is euthymic-compressed, not dysthymic.

### 4.6 Generalized Anxiety Disorder — **Ruled out.** No excessive worry, no muscle tension, no restlessness, no concentration impairment from worry. Her threat-appraisal is *focused* (situational, accurate, time-bound), not generalized.

### 4.7 Panic Disorder — **Ruled out.** Constitutional substrate makes this near-impossible: a body that does not register pain anticipation does not generate panic surges in the autonomic-feedback sense.

### 4.8 Acute Stress Disorder — **Not applicable.** Wrong window; events are years remote.

### 4.9 Adjustment Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.x) — **Not currently met.**

A defensible case could be made for Adjustment Disorder with mixed features around the time-displacement event itself, but the criterion of clinically significant distress or functional impairment is not met. She is functioning; the affective load is contained. Held open as a *latent* candidate if displacement-related stressors compound.

### 4.10 Dissociative Disorders — **Ruled out.**

No dissociative identity phenomena, no fugue, no depersonalization-derealization meeting threshold. The time-displacement situation creates a derealization-shaped *risk pocket* — she is living in a world that her epistemics tell her is not the world she lost — but she is not reporting or behaviorally displaying derealization. Reality testing is intact, sense of self is intact, sense of environment is intact.

The composed-past-tense affect when discussing dead parents could superficially resemble dissociative detachment. It is not. Dissociative detachment includes a sense of unreality, observer-perspective experience, and emotional numbing as a state phenomenon. Hers is suppression as a chosen defense, with the affect available behind the suppression. The clinical distinction holds.

### 4.11 Cluster B Personality Disorders — **Ruled out, categorically.**

- *Narcissistic:* No grandiosity, no entitlement, no need for admiration, no exploitative pattern. She under-claims. She wears Steve Rogers' symbol and does not claim Steve Rogers' status. The opposite of NPD.
- *Borderline:* No identity instability (the role-fused identity is the precise *opposite* of BPD identity diffusion — too narrow, not too unstable), no affective instability, no abandonment fears expressed, no idealization-devaluation pattern, no self-harm, no SI, no chronic emptiness.
- *Histrionic:* No attention-seeking, no theatrical affect, no shallow expressed emotion, no sexualized self-presentation.
- *Antisocial:* No deceitfulness, no impulsivity, no aggression beyond mission-bounded, no irresponsibility, no lack of remorse. She is hyper-responsible, the inverse phenotype.

### 4.12 Cluster A Personality Disorders — **Ruled out.** No suspiciousness, no detachment from social relationships, no eccentricity of cognition or behavior.

### 4.13 Cluster C Personality Disorders — **Subclinical traits only.**

- *Obsessive-Compulsive PD:* Trait-level hyperresponsibility and duty-saturation are present (see §3.1) without disorder threshold. The differentiating factors: she is not rigid, not perfectionistic at task-impeding levels, not preoccupied with rules over outcomes. The hyperresponsibility is OCPD-adjacent in surface texture but lacks the rigidity-core that defines the disorder.
- *Dependent:* Absent. She is the inverse — others depend on her.
- *Avoidant:* Absent. She is socially available and engaged.

### 4.14 Substance Use Disorders — **Ruled out.** No record of use. Constitutional substrate likely makes most substances pharmacokinetically uninteresting to her anyway (the inherited durability/healing implies hepatic and CNS processing rates that resist intoxication).

### 4.15 Eating, Sleep, Sexual, and Neurocognitive Disorders — **No data, no presenting concerns.** The hyperresponsibility pattern would predict sleep economy as a likely subclinical pressure outlet (see §3.1) but no diagnostic threshold reached on available data.

### 4.16 Autism Spectrum / ADHD — **Ruled out.** Social reciprocity is intact and nuanced. No restricted interests beyond mission-appropriate focus. No attentional dysregulation. No sensory profile abnormalities (though the constitutional damped-pain channel could mimic sensory hyporesponsivity — a methodological note for any future evaluator, not a diagnostic finding).

### 4.17 The "Identification with the Aggressor" Differential — **Ruled out.**

Worth naming because it is the wrong-but-tempting read of a child who took up the shield of a dead idealized figure. Anna Freud's construct (identification with the aggressor) describes the child who internalizes the threatening other to neutralize the threat. Steve Rogers was not her aggressor; he was the idealized inheritance. Klein's *introjective identification with the lost object* is the correct frame: she has taken the dead-loved-figure inside as ego-structure. This is mourning's high road, not its perversion.

---

## 5. Comorbidity Analysis

Given the absence of primary disorders, comorbidity is hypothetical. The relevant question is: if a disorder lights up under future stress, what are the likely co-traveling features?

- **If the role is lost → likely co-presentation:** acute adjustment disorder with mixed depressed/anxious features, decompensation of suppressed grief toward PGD-spectrum symptoms, and possible identity-disruption phenomena as the ego scaffolding folds inward. This cluster could meet threshold within weeks of role loss; her constitutional substrate would mute the somatic-anxiety side but not the affective or cognitive sides.
- **If a teammate dies under her command → likely co-presentation:** acute stress features with possible PTSD trajectory if the loss is gruesome or attributable; activation of survivor's-guilt content not present in the parental-loss material (because the parental loss is *not* her responsibility in her own narrative, but a subordinate's death would be).
- **If forced into peacetime → likely co-presentation:** the rare positive-context decompensation. Hyperresponsibility patterns convert poorly to leisure. Adjustment-disorder-with


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: DANIELLE CAGE

*A condition-by-condition catalog of micro-behavior, decision-shape, and tell. Compiled from longitudinal observation across the child record (infancy through approximately age 8 in present-MU continuity) and the adult record (Captain America of 20XX, displaced to present). Where the two records illuminate each other — where the child's pattern becomes the adult's signature — the link is marked.*

---

## 1. BASELINE / CALM

The default state, observable in U.S.Avengers downtime, hangar bays, debrief rooms, and the rare quiet hour. Calm in Subject is not absence of vigilance — it is vigilance dialed to a sustainable wattage.

**Posture and carriage.** Stands at functional attention even when ostensibly at rest: weight evenly distributed, one foot fractionally forward (the lead foot is the right, consistent across the record — bias inherited from her father's blocking stance, not from formal Captain America shield-doctrine which is symmetrical). When seated, sits forward of the chair-back roughly 80% of the time; full recline is rare and reads, when it occurs, as a deliberate signal of trust to the room. Shoulders are squared but not rigid. The neck stays mobile — small involuntary checks every 30–90 seconds toward doorways, windows, and the highest sightline in the room. She does not know she is doing this.

**Hands.** Resting hands almost never go into pockets. The left hand frequently rests on the upper thigh or hip; the right stays free. When seated at a table she keeps both hands above the surface, palms loosely on the wood. This is a Luke-inheritance: a man who spent years inside a system that punished hidden hands.

**Eyes and scan.** Slow saccade, full-room sweep every 45–90 seconds at rest; tighter sweep (every 10–20 seconds) when the perimeter is unfamiliar. Establishes the room's exits within the first 12 seconds of entering — a tell consistent enough to time. Holds eye contact in conversation longer than American baseline by perhaps a beat; does not perform the polite glance-away. This produces an unintended effect of weight, which she has not corrected because she does not perceive it.

**Voice and speech.** Pitched lower than her physiological range; relaxed-Dani speaks higher. Sentence length in calm is medium-long, grammatically complete, low filler-word density ("um," "like," "you know" appear at roughly a quarter the baseline-American rate). She finishes other people's sentences only when the other person is searching for a specific word and visibly struggling — she offers the word, never the thought.

**Micro-tells of contentment.** A brief one-cornered smile that does not reach the eyes is *not* contentment — that is courtesy. Actual contentment shows as: a slight forward chin-drop, a sustained exhale through the nose, and a relaxation of the muscles at the lateral edge of the jaw. Observable perhaps twice in any given week.

**Habits at rest.** Cleans the shield. Not because it needs cleaning — because the motion of cleaning is the motion of accounting for a tool. She rotates it forearm-over-forearm, inspects the rim, runs a cloth along the inside concavity, and sets it down with the star oriented toward the door. Frequency: once daily minimum, usually evening. *Origin (child record):* Luke's habit of checking the apartment locks twice nightly; Jessica's habit of clearing her sidearm before bed even in years she didn't carry one. Subject internalized: end-of-day, one ritual, one tool, one count.

**Reading.** When she reads — and she reads, surprisingly omnivorously — she holds the material at a slight downward angle, head level, eyes tracking down. She does not bring books to her face. This keeps the peripheral field open.

---

## 2. UNDER LOW STRESS (Pressure without Threat)

Briefing rooms. Difficult conversations. Press contact. Bureaucratic friction.

**Verbal compression.** Sentences shorten by approximately one-third. Filler words drop to near zero. She replaces qualifiers ("I think," "probably," "maybe") with declaratives. The shift is unmistakable to anyone who has logged thirty hours of her speech.

**Hand stillness.** Her hands stop doing the small ambient things calm-hands do (small adjustments of cuff, glass, hair). They settle. Total stillness in the hands while the face remains animated is her single most reliable low-stress tell.

**The pause before the answer.** In calm conversation she answers at conversational tempo. Under low stress she introduces a deliberate half-second pause before responding to any question that has decision-weight. She is not buying time to think — she has already thought; she is buying time to *decide what to share*. The pause is the gate.

**Disagreement style.** She does not raise her voice to disagree. She lowers it. The drop of perhaps a quarter-octave is consistent enough to be diagnostic. She frames disagreement as a question first ("Is that the read?") and only states her counter-position if the question is dismissed. *Origin:* Jessica's tradecraft — never tip your hand on the first move; let the other party recommit to their position before you take it apart.

**Bureaucratic stress.** Forms, requisitions, chain-of-command friction visibly tax her more than combat. She handles it by completing the task in one uninterrupted sitting rather than rationing it. She has been observed signing forty-seven pages of incident paperwork in a single ninety-minute block with one bathroom break. The expression during such work is the closest she comes to ordinary irritation: a tightening at the bridge of the nose, a slight forward set of the lower jaw.

---

## 3. UNDER ACUTE STRESS (Active Crisis, Pre-Combat)

The minutes before contact. Intelligence is coming in. The plan is forming. Lives are on the table.

**Affect compression.** Her face does what most operators' faces do under pre-combat load — it goes quiet — but with a specific signature: the mouth softens rather than tightens. Most operators clench. She *releases* the perioral musculature. The effect is a face that looks almost serene at the moment others look grim. This is not performance; it is a deeply internalized regulation. *Origin:* observed in her father across the child record — Luke's pre-fight face is calm to the point of opacity. Subject mirrored it before she could form sentences.

**Decision tempo.** Accelerates. Calm-Dani deliberates in seconds; acute-stress-Dani decides in fractions. Her decisions in this state are demonstrably good but *not optimized* — she trades five percent of solution quality for sixty percent of decision speed, and she has the self-awareness to know this is the right trade. She has been heard to say, post-action, "We had a better option. We didn't have time for it." Said without self-flagellation.

**Triage instinct.** The first thing she does in any multi-victim, multi-threat situation is *count*. Civilians first, then combatants, then teammates, then exits. The count happens silently and visibly: her gaze flicks in a specific pattern, left-to-right across the lower visual field (civilians, who are usually closer to the ground — fallen, crouching, fleeing), then upper field (threats, who are usually standing/elevated), then teammates (whose positions she already knows), then ingress/egress.

**Order-giving.** Short sentences, names first, verbs second. "Toni, left flank. Aikku, civilians. Sam, with me." She uses given names rather than callsigns. *Origin:* Luke's "we are people, not assets" doctrine, absorbed in childhood. Even in extremis she refuses to dehumanize her team into function-handles.

**Shield handling.** In pre-contact she does not hold the shield ready. She holds it loose, at her side, the rim resting against her outer thigh. This is a tell to those who know her: shield-loose means she has not yet decided whether the encounter will be combat. The instant the shield comes up to the forearm-bracket, the decision has been made and is irrevocable.

**Breathing.** Drops to a four-count inhale, six-count exhale. Audible only at close range. She does this without conscious instruction now, but the count was learned — somewhere in the displaced timeline, someone taught it to her, and she has carried it back.

---

## 4. IN COMBAT

The most-observed state. The state in which the body of inheritance does its inheriting.

**Movement architecture.** She fights low. Her center of gravity stays under most opponents'. This is a smaller-fighter's habit — significant because she is *not* a smaller fighter; her strength baseline is at or above her father's. She fights as if she were vulnerable, which makes her tactically harder to read. *Origin (inference):* trained against opponents in the future timeline who outclassed her strength; the low-center habit predates her full power expression and was retained.

**Strike economy.** Does not throw flurries. Single committed strikes, with full recovery between. Two-to-three-strike combinations only when the target is already compromised. This is a Luke-pattern — the man who hits once because he only needs to hit once — modified by a Captain America-trained sense of *non-lethality*: she pulls strikes against unenhanced opponents with a precision that suggests considerable practice with the calibration.

**Shield use.** Three observable modes:
- *Defensive bracket* — shield up, forearm braced, used as mobile cover. Her default in civilian-dense environments.
- *Strike platform* — shield as edge-weapon and bludgeon. Used against armored or enhanced threats.
- *Thrown* — comparatively rare in her hands. She throws the shield perhaps one-fifth as often as her predecessor reportedly did. The reason is visible in her face when she throws it: a flicker of reluctance to relinquish the tool. The shield, for her, is partly a held-object identification — releasing it is a small relinquishment of the inheritance she is wearing.

**Talk in combat.** Minimal. What there is, is directional ("On your six." "Down." "Hold."). She does not banter. She does not threaten opponents. She does not announce her strikes. The silence is itself a tell to opponents accustomed to costumed bravado — they often misread it as inexperience and learn otherwise.

**Pain response.** Muted, both because she largely doesn't feel it and because the few times something *does* break through (energy weapons, magic, the rare strike that registers), her response is a sharp single exhale followed by no further acknowledgment. She does not check the wound. She does not look at her own body. She continues.

**Killing.** Has not, on record, killed. Has demonstrated calibrated capacity to incapacitate at extreme power-bandwidth without lethal outcome. The discipline reads as load-bearing — there is a sense, visible in the millisecond restraint of her heaviest strikes, that she has made killing a line and will not be the one to move it. *Inference:* she has, in the future timeline, faced the temptation and chosen against it; she carries the choice as identity.

---

## 5. POST-COMBAT / DECOMPRESSION

The hour after the fight. The most psychologically revealing window in any operator's day.

**The shield-set.** First action upon return to safe perimeter: set the shield down. Not on a rack. On a surface — table, bench, floor — flat, star-up. The placement is ritual. She does not rest until it is done. *Origin (inference):* a child's habit of putting a toy down in a specific way before moving on, retained and weaponized as adult ritual.

**Headcount.** Second action: lays eyes on every member of the team. Not by name-check — by *visual confirmation*. She walks the line, looks at each face, briefly touches a shoulder or forearm of those she is closest to. The touch is consistent: outer left shoulder, brief, two-second contact. She does this even with teammates uninjured and visibly fine. *Origin:* documented in the child record — toddler-Dani, returning home with a parent after an absence, would touch each adult in the apartment in turn before settling. The behavior survived to adulthood unchanged in structure.

**Hydration.** Drinks water in large measured pulls, not sips. She tracks her own hydration with discipline. Will not eat for forty-five to sixty minutes after combat — the appetite is suppressed and she does not force it.

**Debrief tempo.** Wants the debrief soon, not late. Will lead it within ninety minutes of action-end if permitted. Her stated reason ("while it's fresh") is operationally true; the *psychological* reason is that the debrief is the metabolizing ritual — the conversion of event into accounted-for record. Unaccounted-for events are what she does not tolerate.

**Solitude window.** After debrief, requires roughly forty minutes alone before re-engaging socially. Spends it on physical maintenance — shield care, equipment check, a shower run long and hot. Does not journal. Does not call anyone. Does not look at photographs.

---

## 6. UNDER THREAT TO SELF (Personal Danger, Non-Mission)

Ambush, assassination attempt, personal targeting.

**Initial response: stillness.** Her first reaction to personal threat is to *not move*. A full beat — perhaps half a second — of total motionlessness while assessment completes. This is unusual. Most operators flinch or pivot; she calibrates. The stillness is so brief most observers miss it, but it is consistent.

**Disengagement bias.** Given the option, she will disengage from a personal-target situation rather than escalate. Not from fear — from a refusal to let her own person become the operational center. She does not believe she is the priority. *Origin:* a childhood in which she was, repeatedly, the priority — and watched what that cost her parents. Adult-Dani has organized her self-concept around *not being the thing that has to be protected*.

**If cornered:** competence ratchets up rather than panic. The face goes still. The breathing drops to the four-six count. The shield comes up. She does not announce. She fights.

---

## 7. UNDER THREAT TO TEAM / LOVED PERIMETER

A different state entirely. The pressure-point axis.

**Voice rises.** This is the *only* condition under which her voice rises rather than drops. It does not become shrill — it becomes carrying. She uses the volume to take command of a chaotic field. Three or four words at this volume, then she drops back to operational pitch.

**Movement aggressiveness.** Closes distance to the threatened party. Will not snipe from cover when someone she is responsible for is exposed; will move *to* them, place herself between, and absorb. The shield comes up high and angled — covering the protected party's upper mass first, her own second.

**Risk tolerance ceiling collapses.** Decisions that would take a deliberate half-second in personal-threat take nothing in team-threat. She has been observed running through a line of fire to reach a downed teammate without checking suppression. She knows she does this. She has not corrected it. She has, in private debrief, acknowledged it as her "known liability." That she names it suggests she has decided to keep it.

---

## 8. IN INTIMACY (Non-Sexual: Close Friendship, Family, Trust-Bonds)

A relatively underdeveloped domain in her observable record. The signal-to-noise is sparse because the situations are sparse.

**With teammates she has accepted as chosen-family:** physical proximity tolerance rises substantially. She will sit shoulder-to-shoulder on a bench, share a small kitchen space, allow casual contact (a hand on her arm to get her attention, a teammate leaning briefly against her). She does not initiate this contact; she *permits* it, and the permission is unmistakable as warmth rather than passivity.

**With present-day Luke and Jessica.** This is the diagnostic case. Adult-Dani's behavior around her living, present-tense parents is *the most controlled set of micro-behaviors on her record*. She maintains a specific physical distance — roughly arm's-plus-elbow, not embrace-range. She does not initiate hugs. She uses their names ("Luke," "Jessica") rather than parental terms. Her eye contact with them is slightly briefer than her standard. She smiles more frequently than her baseline when speaking with them, and the smile is *not* the contentment-smile; it is the courtesy-smile, deployed as a buffer.

What she *does* do: she watches them when they are not looking at her. The watching is the unguarded behavior. She does not know she does this. It is the single largest break in her otherwise-flawless containment.

**With present-day child-Dani (if/when proximate).** Behaviorally unparseable; canon underdraws this contact. Inference: she would not let it happen if she could avoid it.

---

## 9. IN INTIMACY (Romantic / Sexual)

Sparse to absent in the canonical record. The behavior is therefore inferred from adjacent patterns and stated absences.

**Likely pattern.** Mission-mediated bonds preferred. Will form deep attachment to a peer-operator more readily than to a non-combatant. The models she was raised by — her parents — bonded in shared crisis and stayed bonded through it; her template for intimate partnership is *co-combatant*, not *companion*. Civilian partners would likely register, at some level she might not consciously articulate, as people she would have to protect, which is the wrong axis for her to relax into intimacy on.

**Low-stakes social/romantic registers** — parties, dating, ordinary courtship — would be a markedly underdeveloped competency. She has not had the developmental years in which baseline-humans practice these registers. Her late-teens and early adulthood, in the displaced timeline, were spent in survival and inheritance.

**Sexual behavior tells.** Unobserved on record. Reasonable inference: high control of disclosure, deliberate rather than impulsive, partner-attentive in the manner of someone whose default mode is *responsibility for the perimeter*.

---

## 10. IN GRIEF

The most carefully managed state. The state for which all her defenses were built.

**Acute grief (teammate death, mission failure with loss of life).** External presentation: she stays *operational*. She delivers the relevant communications — to family, to command, to the team — herself, on the assumption that the person who held the command holds the cost. Her voice in these communications is steady. The tell is in the pacing: she speaks more slowly than her baseline. The slowdown is not for the listener; it is for her own respiration.

**Physical correlates.** Appetite drops. Sleep shortens. The shield-cleaning ritual extends — twice-daily, longer sessions. She runs more (she runs daily already; under grief, the runs lengthen by perhaps fifty percent). She does not cry in observable settings. Inference: she cries in the shower, where the somatic and acoustic signatures are masked; this is a constructed privacy, almost certainly deliberate.

**Recovery curve.** Functional recovery within forty-eight to seventy-two hours. *True* recovery probably never completed — she does not reprocess; she stores. The storage is the structure her adult identity is built around. The lost are kept inside the role she inherited from them.

**Anniversary behavior.** Inferred but consistent with profile: she would mark dates privately, by act rather than ceremony — a particular run route, a particular hour spent on shield maintenance, a particular silence.

**The parents-grief.** Held since adolescence (precise age at loss not specified in canon; behavioral evidence suggests mid-to-late teens). Integrated by introjection — she carries them by being who they would be. The integration is functional and stable. The seams have not been stress-tested by, for example, encountering an alternate-timeline version of either parent in mortal danger; if such a situation occurred, the prediction is that her containment would hold operationally but cost her a measurable interval of post-event recovery.

---

## 11. IN VICTORY

A surprisingly muted state. Victory does not produce the affect-expansion most observers expect.

**Immediate response to a won fight.** A single nod. Sometimes to a teammate, sometimes to no one — an acknowledgment to the moment itself. She does not pump fists. She does not whoop. She does not high-five (will return one if offered, with a deliberate completeness that suggests she has practiced reciprocating expressions she does not generate).

**Smile in victory.** The contentment-smile, not the courtesy-smile, appears more often in victory than in any other condition. Brief. Real. Often directed at a specific teammate rather than the room.

**Tendency to credit-distribute.** In any debrief or public statement following success, she names her team's contributions before her own and frequently omits her own entirely. This is not false modesty; it is operationally accurate by her own accounting — *she does not consider command contribution to be her own action*. She believes she facilitated; they acted. The team has tried, repeatedly, to correct this. She receives the correction politely and does not change.

**Post-victory celebration.** Will attend. Will stay roughly ninety minutes. Will drink moderately (one drink, possibly two over a long evening; never beyond first-edge of intoxication — her physiology may or may not permit it, but the behavioral discipline is consistent). Will leave before the rest of the team and not announce her leaving.

---

## 12. IN DEFEAT

The least-observed state because it is the state she has been most spared. Inference is heavier here.

**Immediate response to a lost fight (survival case).** Composes the after-action picture before composing herself. Headcount, casualty assessment, secure perimeter, evac coordination. She will not allow herself to *feel* the defeat until the operational sequence is closed.

**Self-blame.** Substantial and largely silent. The pattern is to absorb command-responsibility for outcome regardless of distributed causation. She will, in debrief, accept attributions of fault she does not actually own — not from passivity but from a stated belief that the commander wears the loss. *Origin:* probable inheritance from her displaced-timeline experience of being the symbol on whom outcomes converged.

**Public face.** Holds. Public statements following defeat are calibrated to take heat off the team and onto the role.

**Private face.** Inferred: extends every solitude ritual. Sleeps less. Runs more. Cleans the shield with abnormal frequency. Does not, on record, drink to excess; the behavioral pattern argues against it as a coping route.

**Recurrence risk.** A serial defeat or a single catastrophic one would be the most likely trigger for her latent decompensation. The role-as-identity is built to weather episodic failure; it is not built to weather *invalidation of the role itself*. Removing her from command, decommissioning the shield, or convincing her that her stewardship was net-harmful would constitute the actual existential threat to her.

---

## 13. UNDER DECEPTION / SOCIAL MANIPULATION

A category in which her mother's inheritance shows most clearly.

**Detection.** Above-baseline reliable. She listens to *what* is said and tracks the *order* in which it is said. Inconsistencies of sequence — facts presented out of the natural narrative order — register on her face as a brief tightening at the outer corner of the right eye. She does not call out the inconsistency in the moment. She files it and tests it later.

**Counter-deception.** She does not lie well in low-stakes registers — she has been raised to value clean speech and her default is declarative. In *operational* contexts she can run a clean cover; the difference is permission. She lies on mission because the mission has authorized it. She will not lie in personal contexts and has been observed declining to participate in even small social fictions (surprise parties, polite untruths) with a quiet refusal that reads as principle rather than awkwardness.

**Manipulation attempts on her.** Pass through her low-defense layer (she is approachable, warm, available) and hit a hard floor underneath (mission-priority, ethical anchor, team-protection). The visible
